# Peter Parker — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

*UATU FILE — PARKER, PETER BENJAMIN. Subject designation: SPIDER-MAN. Compiled from sixty-plus years of behavioral record. Section 0 of full dossier. Read this before anything else; the remainder of the file substantiates what follows.*

---

## 0.1 Bottom Line, Up Front

The subject is a constitutionally sensitive, high-intelligence male, now in his mid-to-late twenties by the most stable in-canon dating but with a behavioral record spanning six decades of publication, in whom a single forty-eight-hour adolescent sequence — the acquisition of superhuman capacity, a deliberate moral abdication (refusing to stop a fleeing thief), and the murder of his surrogate father by that same thief — fused **guilt and identity** into a single load-bearing structure that has organized every subsequent decision of his life. He is not, at root, a hero who suffers. He is **a survivor of an unmetabolized adolescent guilt event who has converted that guilt into a permanent vocation of preemptive rescue**, and who has, over roughly fifteen in-universe years and sixty publication years, refined that conversion into an ethical practice of unusual integrity and considerable personal cost.

Everything else in this file — the quip, the lateness, the serial romantic rupture, the chronic insolvency, the masochistic absorption of injury, the no-kill absolutism, the inability to metabolize praise, the marriage trade to a metaphysical entity to save his aunt, the willingness to surrender his own body to prevent a death — is downstream of that single fusion. The subject is **not complex in his drivers; he is complex in his compensations.** The driver is one wound, held open for sixty years by a defense system that prevents healing because healing would require accepting that he is not, in fact, the cause of every death he failed to prevent — and accepting that would dismantle the moral architecture on which his entire prosocial output is built. He cannot put down the load without becoming someone who never carried it, and he experiences the prospect of that man with horror.

He is, in plain language, **a person who is permanently atoning for a sin whose proportional weight he assigned himself at fifteen and has refused, on principle, to renegotiate.**

---

## 0.2 The Through-Line

If the file is reduced to one sentence: **Peter Parker is a boy who, at fifteen, decided that the price of his guilt was his entire life, and has spent every day since paying the bill on time.**

If reduced to two: **The capacity is borrowed; the conscience is native. The capacity made the conscience operational at a scale no fifteen-year-old should be asked to carry, and he carried it anyway, and is still carrying it, and the carrying is now the man.**

The through-line across every era of the record — the early Lee/Ditko adolescence of scapegoated isolation, the Lee/Romita young-adult stabilization, the Conway-era catastrophic loss of Gwen Stacy, the DeMatteis interior excavations (the Kraven burial, the Harry Osborn sequences), the Michelinie/McFarlane romantic stabilization with Mary Jane, the clone-saga identity rupture, the Straczynski mystical-totemic recontextualization, the Civil War public unmasking, the One More Day marital sacrifice, the Slott Superior body-theft and its aftermath, the Spencer attempts at restitution — is a single repeated structural move: **when forced to choose between his own integrity-of-self and the survival of an attachment figure, he trades the self every time, without visible deliberation, and then improvises a rationalization afterward.** The improvisation is sometimes elegant ("with great power…"), sometimes desperate (the bargain with Mephisto), sometimes catastrophic (the Registration sign-on, then reversal), but the *underlying trade* is invariant. It is the trade he failed to make for Ben — the trade of his own evening, his own ego-gratification at the wrestling purse, his own indifference, in exchange for the two seconds of intervention that would have stopped the thief — and he has been making that trade preemptively, for everyone, ever since.

This is the load. It is not heroism in the classical sense (the seeking of glory through risk), nor in the religious sense (obedience to a calling), nor in the existentialist sense (the assertion of meaning against absurdity). It is **restitutionary**. He is paying back a debt to a dead man through proxies, and the debt does not decrease because the creditor is unreachable.

---

## 0.3 Who He Is at the Deepest Level

Strip the costume, the powers, the rogues' gallery, the cosmic-totem retcons, the alternate-reality variants. What remains is this:

**A temperamentally sensitive only child, prematurely orphaned, raised inside love organized by anxiety, who learned three things before age twelve that have never been unlearned:** (1) the people who love you can vanish without warning and without explanation; (2) you cannot burden the people who remain, because they too are fragile; (3) intelligence is the one currency that reliably purchases approval, and it is therefore to be cultivated in lieu of all softer goods. By the time the spider bit him, the personality structure was already set: hyper-verbal, hyper-cognitive, affectively walled-off behind a thin performance of indifference, attachment-hungry but attachment-terrified, with a moral sense already disproportionate to his age and a self-concept already organized around inadequacy.

The bite did not change who he was. **The bite gave a fifteen-year-old with that personality structure the physical capacity to act on the moral imperative that personality structure had already been generating for years without an outlet.** This is the most underappreciated fact in the file. The spider conferred adhesion, strength, reflex, and proprioception. It did not confer the conscience. The conscience was already there, weaponized and waiting, with no target. Ben's death gave it the target. The target has expanded since (the city, the world, the multiverse in the cosmic arcs) but the *operation* has not changed: locate harm, prevent harm, accept all costs of prevention as just, accept any failure of prevention as personally damning.

At the deepest level he is therefore **a moral instrument with a human being attached** — and the human being is, by his own internal account, the lesser of the two. He privately experiences "Spider-Man" as the part of him that works correctly and "Peter" as the part that is always failing — failing rent, failing dates, failing classes, failing May, failing MJ, failing to be the man Ben would have wanted. This bifurcation is the engine of the so-called Parker Luck. The luck is not luck; it is the predictable downstream of a self-concept that experiences personal stability as morally unearned and therefore arranges, mostly outside conscious awareness, for that stability to collapse. He is not unlucky. He is **arranging the punishment that he believes the original sin requires** and that the universe has, irritatingly, declined to deliver.

Beneath the performance — beneath the warmth, the wit, the genuine generosity, the verbal disarmament that nearly everyone who meets him remarks on — he is **lonely in a precise, irreducible way**: lonely for the parents he cannot remember, lonely for the uncle whose death he believes he caused, lonely for the version of himself who might have grown up without the load. He does not name this loneliness even to himself. Naming it would require putting the load down to look at it, and he has not been able to do that since 1962.

---

## 0.4 The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

**The core wound** is not Ben's death. The core wound is the **structural fusion of moral identity with the act of omission that preceded Ben's death**. Ben died because of the thief's bullet. Peter knows this intellectually. The wound is that he experienced the death not as something that happened *to* him but as something he *did* — by inaction, by indifference, by the prior selfish use of his powers for the wrestling money. The fusion was set in the forty-eight hours of *Amazing Fantasy* #15: power → selfishness → omission → death of the loved one. The equation, once written into a fifteen-year-old's identity at the developmental moment when identity is most plastic, became axiomatic. He has never disputed it. Every subsequent loss (Captain Stacy, Gwen Stacy, Jean DeWolff, Marla Jameson, the temporary loss of May) re-substantiates the equation and adds a term. Every save discharges interest on the principal but does not touch the principal.

**Maintenance of the wound is performed by an integrated defense complex with the following components, each of which prevents the wound from healing while permitting the subject to remain functional:**

- **The quip.** Manic-defense / reaction-formation hybrid. At the precise moment affect would surface (fear, grief, rage), the verbal apparatus produces its opposite (levity, mockery, absurdity). The quip is genuine in that it reflects actual wit and actual warmth; it is defensive in that its *timing* is governed by affect intensity, not by social cue. Foes have identified this (Venom, Kingpin, Octavius); allies have named it (the Human Torch, Daredevil, MJ herself). Functionally, the quip is the regulation skill he was never taught and improvised — effective at preventing collapse, costly in that it precludes processing.

- **Motion.** Web-swinging is depicted, by nearly every artist who has drawn him, as the only time his face is at rest. Movement at altitude through the city is, for this subject, the functional equivalent of what running is for endurance athletes with anxiety disorders: a kinesthetic-cardiovascular regulation channel that displaces affect into musculature and air. When motion is denied (the Kraven burial, restraints, the Superior body-theft) the underlying state surfaces and it is depressive, ruminative, and suicidally tinged.

- **Work.** Dual and sometimes triple occupational load (photography, science teaching, lab work, freelance R&D depending on era) plus the unpaid second life of patrol. Work is not income strategy; income strategy is, in fact, conspicuously absent. Work is **continuous self-justification through visible utility**. Idleness is intolerable because idleness allows the wound to be felt.

- **Secret-keeping as relational regulator.** The secret identity is operationally necessary (enemies would target loved ones) but psychologically *over-performed* — he keeps it from people he could safely tell, discloses to people in moments calibrated to test their loyalty, and unconsciously uses the secret as the wedge that ruptures relationships when intimacy reaches the threshold his attachment system cannot tolerate. The Mary Jane exception (she identified him independently and chose him *with* the knowledge) is the only relational configuration that has stabilized, precisely because it neutralizes the secret as instrument.

- **Hypertrophied responsibility-assumption.** Any harm in his proximity is metabolized as his harm. This is not philosophy; it is reflex. It accepts no contrary evidence. The "with great power" formula is the rationalization scaffolding atop the reflex, not its source.

- **Refusal of the lethal solution.** The no-kill absolutism is held even against Carnage, even against Osborn post-Gwen, even against Kraven, even against Octavius after the body-theft. It looks deontological from the outside. Internally, it is **prophylactic**: to kill once would be to confirm that he is the kind of person whose action ends lives, which is what he privately believes he already became at fifteen. The rule keeps the equation from completing. It is, in this frame, less a moral commitment than a containment vessel.

- **The body as ledger.** Injury is absorbed without recourse to caution. He is shot, stabbed, burned, broken, has clinically died at least twice, operates on chronic sleep deprivation and insufficient caloric intake against an enhanced metabolic load. The body is not protected because protecting it would imply he believes it is worth protecting in the proportion the rescue calculus demands. Damage to the self is the only form of payment the wound accepts as legitimate.

The defense complex is *successful*. It has kept the subject functional, prosocial, ethically coherent, and creatively productive across six decades of stressors that have produced measurable ethical drift in comparable subjects (Stark, Richards, Banner). It is also *self-perpetuating*. Each component prevents the wound from being felt long enough to be metabolized, which keeps the wound active, which sustains demand for the component. The notable absence of chemical self-medication (no drinking to excess, no recreational drug use — a contrast Stan Lee deliberately built against the Harry Osborn arc, ASM #96–98) is diagnostic: the defense complex is robust enough that pharmacology is unnecessary. He is, in effect, **self-medicating with vocation at therapeutic dose**.

---

## 0.5 Operational Summary

For purposes of any operator, ally, handler, adversary, or analyst working from this file, the following operational characteristics should be treated as load-bearing:

**Reliability.** Extraordinary in life-safety domains, poor in scheduled-mundane domains. He will appear, without fail, when a life is in danger and he is reachable. He will *not* reliably appear for dinner, class, meetings, or appointments unless the personal cost of missing them has already been internalized as a moral failure on par with the rescue calculus. Plan accordingly. Build redundancy around scheduled commitments. Do not build redundancy around emergency response — he is the redundancy.

**Decision-making under threat.** Fast, accurate, ethically constrained, and biased toward absorbing personal cost. He will reliably underweight his own survival relative to the survival of any present civilian, and will reliably refuse the lethal option even when it is operationally indicated. Tactical planning involving him should assume both.

**Decision-making under intimacy.** Slow, anxious, avoidant, prone to preemptive rupture. He will reliably *over*-weight the risk of burdening a loved one and *under*-weight the cost to them of being kept at distance. Relational planning involving him should assume distance-regulation behavior under conditions of increasing closeness; the appropriate intervention is patient persistence past the rupture point, not pursuit of immediate disclosure.

**Verbal output as diagnostic.** Quip frequency and intensity are inversely correlated with regulated affect. A talkative Spider-Man is a Spider-Man under load. A *silent* Spider-Man is a Spider-Man either tactically constrained or in genuine crisis; the silent state is the one to attend to, not the loud state.

**Pressure points, in descending order of severity.**
1. Direct threat to May Parker, Mary Jane, or any surrogate-dependent (Anna Maria, alternate-reality daughter figures). Bypasses all tactical judgment. He will accept any operational cost, including catastrophic ones, to neutralize the threat.
2. Forced immobilization or compelled spectatorship of harm. The single condition under which his defense complex fails completely. Villains who have discovered this (Kraven, Osborn at peak, Octavius) have produced his worst documented decompensations.
3. Accusation of irresponsibility, from any source including enemies. Lands as true because internally pre-confirmed. Can be exploited for short-term destabilization; should not be exploited by anyone who wishes to remain in his good graces.
4. Public exposure of identity. Triggers destabilization disproportionate to the practical consequences because the bifurcated self-system requires the wall between selves to function. The Civil War sequence is the type case.
5. Sincere, sustained praise. Paradoxically destabilizing. Acceptance would require revising the foundational failure-self-concept. He will deflect with humor and exit the situation if possible.

**Allies and handlers should expect:** lateness; financial precarity (declined offers of money, repeatedly, including from Stark and Richards, sources he could plausibly accept from); intermittent withdrawal followed by reliable re-emergence at the moment of crisis; warmth that is genuine but does not preclude rupture; total candor on tactical questions and total opacity on personal ones; an apparently inexhaustible supply of self-blame that should not be reinforced by careless framing.

**Adversaries should expect:** moral predictability (he will not kill, he will not let civilians die, he will accept personal cost to prevent both), tactical unpredictability (the high-g engineering mind is genuinely creative under pressure), increasing focal intensity the closer the threat moves to his attachment figures, and an inability to be psychologically broken by any means short of attacking those attachment figures directly — at which point he is, briefly and predictably, the most dangerous version of himself, and the only version of himself who could plausibly cross the no-kill line.

**Long-horizon trajectory.** The subject has demonstrated, over the documented sixty years, a remarkable refusal to ethically drift. He has not become Stark; he has not become Richards; he has not become Banner. He has remained, recognizably, the same boy who decided at fifteen that the load was his. The cost of that stability is the foreclosed life — the stable career he could have had, the marriage that was traded away, the children not had, the recreation not taken, the rest not slept. Whether the trade is worth it is not for this file to adjudicate. **That the trade has been honored every day for sixty years, without renegotiation, against every available pressure to renegotiate, is the single most striking datum in the entire file** and should be carried forward into every subsequent section.

---

## 0.6 One-Line Operational Characterization

**Subject is a guilt-organized altruist of unusual moral integrity and considerable personal cost, operating an effective but self-perpetuating defense complex (humor, motion, work, secret-keeping, body-as-ledger) atop an unmetabolized adolescent guilt fusion that he is structurally unable to dismantle without dismantling the prosocial output the dismantling would, in fact, free him to enjoy.**

He is, in the final accounting, **the rare subject in whom the pathology and the virtue are the same structure, viewed from opposite sides.** Treat the structure with care. It is load-bearing for him, for the people he loves, and — the record genuinely supports this claim — for a non-trivial number of the people who are alive in his city because he has not yet permitted himself to rest.

— END EXECUTIVE BRIEF —


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

*UATU Dossier, Section 1 of the longitudinal chronology. Covering: in-utero through approximately age fifteen, terminating at the threshold of the spider bite (Amazing Fantasy #15, August 1962, modernized referent). All entries cross-referenced to canonical source. Inferences flagged as inference; observed behavior cited.*

---

## 1.1 BIRTH AND IN-UTERO CONTEXT

The subject was born to Richard Laurence Parker and Mary Fitzpatrick Parker, a marriage of two intelligence-community professionals whose careers required sustained absence, plausible deniability, and the cultivation, even at home, of a controlled informational perimeter. Richard's CIA service and Mary's parallel role (the latter retconned forward across *Untold Tales of Spider-Man* #-1, *Amazing Spider-Man* #-1, the Mackie/Byrne *Spider-Man: Chapter One* and subsequent *Trail of the Spider* material) establish the relevant fact: the household into which the subject was born was, from the first day, a household structured around the management of secrets. Even in infancy he was the proximate object of a parental discipline that was not principally about him — his caregivers were attentive but oriented elsewhere, and the home itself was geographically unstable (the Parkers' postings included Algiers per *ASM* #-1).

There is no canonical record of birth complications, gestational pathology, or any neonatal datum that would suggest constitutional vulnerability arising from the perinatal window. The constitutional sensitivity that the clinical synthesis identifies (a temperamentally reactive nervous system, easily startled, slow to soothe in social novelty) appears, on the evidence, to be inherited temperament rather than acquired insult — Richard is depicted in flashback as quiet, watchful, given to long silences, and Mary as the more verbally fluent of the pair, both attributes the subject would later display in characteristic combination.

## 1.2 LOSS OF PARENTS

The age at which the subject was orphaned is canonically inconsistent — variously rendered as infancy (*ASM* #-1, the dominant version) or as roughly six years old (the Mackie reboot continuity, which is partially deprecated). The dominant continuity matters more clinically than the deprecated version, because it establishes the controlling fact: **the subject has no consolidated autobiographical memory of his parents**. He inherited their absence, not their presence. Their plane was downed (overtly by Albert Malik, the second Red Skull, per *ASM* #-1); the official cover story given to Aunt May and Uncle Ben and, through them, to the child, was a simple aviation accident.

Two consequences follow and are visible across the entire subsequent canon:

1. **A foundational void where attachment templates are typically laid down.** The subject did not lose parents he could mourn; he lost a category of relationship he never experienced. This produces, in the developmental record, an unusually intense investment in the substitute (Ben and May), and a lifelong inability to tolerate the loss of substitutes — because each substitute is, structurally, also the original.

2. **An early-installed assumption that the truth about important things is withheld.** May and Ben told him his parents had died in a crash; they did not tell him what they did, because they themselves likely did not know in full. The subject grew up inside an information asymmetry centered on himself, and his later, characteristic intolerance of being lied to *about* himself (visible in the Civil War repudiation of Stark, in his reaction to the body-theft, in the Mephisto bargain's downstream resentments) reads as the mature expression of a wound formed here.

## 1.3 RELOCATION TO FOREST HILLS

The subject was placed with Ben and May Parker, Ben being Richard's older brother, at the family residence at 20 Ingram Street, Forest Hills, Queens (canonical address per *ASM* #18 and stable across decades; later rendered as 20 Ingram Court in some renderings). The house — a small, two-story, pre-war wood-frame with a finished basement, an attic, a narrow yard, a back stoop, and a single-car driveway — is, with the FDR Drive and the Brooklyn Bridge, one of the three most canonically depicted physical spaces in the subject's entire life. Its layout has consequences:

- **The basement** became the subject's de facto laboratory by approximately age ten (depicted in *Untold Tales of Spider-Man* #1 and as established backstory in *AF* #15's opening panels). The configuration — descend a flight, close a door, work alone — established the architectural template for his lifelong pattern of *physical withdrawal into a confined enclosed space to do focused intellectual work as a substitute for affect processing*. He has reproduced this template in every subsequent residence (the Chelsea apartment, the Tri-Corp lab, Horizon Labs, Parker Industries, the Coffee Bean back booth).
- **The attic** held his parents' effects — the suitcase containing Richard's files that he would not encounter until adolescence (*ASM* #-1; *Trail of the Spider*).
- **The kitchen**, with May at the stove, is the visual unit of warmth in his early memory; the kitchen is also where bad news has been delivered to him repeatedly across his life (Ben's death; multiple May hospitalizations).

## 1.4 BEN PARKER — THE PRIMARY MALE ATTACHMENT

Benjamin Parker was, by the consistent depiction of Lee, Ditko, Romita, DeFalco, Busiek (*Untold Tales*), Straczynski, and Slott, a working-class autodidact: warm, verbal, given to aphorism, fond of corny humor, devoted to May, devoted to the boy. He worked variously as a carnival barker in his youth (*Untold Tales*), and in later years held a series of unstable jobs typical of his era and class. The household was financially precarious throughout the subject's childhood — this is the second formative environmental variable, and it cannot be overstated. **Money was always a problem.** The subject's later inability to hold a job, ironically, is not an inability to *value* money; it is the opposite — money is so emotionally loaded for him that earning it cleanly and keeping it triggers guilt.

Ben's pedagogical style with the boy was indirect, narrative, and morally framed. The famous "great power" formulation, attributed by *AF* #15's caption (and later directly to Ben in retcon by *ASM* #94 and definitively by Romita Sr.'s reworking) is consistent with the broader pattern: Ben taught through proverbs, stories about his own youth, and small instructive episodes (the bicycle-repair lesson in *Untold Tales* #1; the bullies-and-fishing story in DeMatteis' *The Pulse: House of M*). He did not lecture; he illustrated. The subject's later moral cognition — episodic, exemplar-driven, narratively organized, rarely abstract or rule-deductive — is recognizably Ben's transmission.

Ben took the boy to the cinema (the canonical detail of the old Hollywood films and Westerns, *ASM* #181's flashback), to ballgames (the Mets reference is consistent across decades), and to the Coney Island boardwalk (*Untold Tales*). The recurrent leitmotif is two-person outings — Ben and the boy, no one else, low-cost, repeated, ritualized. These shared rituals are the developmental substrate for the subject's later capacity for the durable male friendship (Johnny Storm, Matt Murdock, Harry Osborn at his best) — he can do this, because he learned to do it.

## 1.5 MAY PARKER — THE PRIMARY FEMALE ATTACHMENT AND THE FRAGILITY ARCHITECTURE

May Reilly Parker, depicted across the Lee/Ditko run as already elderly in apparent age at the time the subject is fifteen (a continuity oddity later softened in JMS' and Slott's runs), is the second pole of the attachment system and the more clinically consequential of the two. May is presented from her earliest appearances as **physically fragile and prone to anxiety**: cardiac complaints (referenced from *ASM* #1 onward), recurrent hospitalizations (*ASM* #9, #31–33, #196–200, #400 most famously), a thinness of frame and tremor of hand that Ditko emphasized and that every subsequent artist has preserved.

The clinically operative pattern is not the physical frailty itself but its **interactional consequence**: the boy learned, before age ten, that his upsets upset May, and that May upset risks May ill, and May ill risks May *dying*. The transitive chain — my feeling → her feeling → her body → her death — is the load-bearing structure of his entire affect regulation. By the time the spider bites him, the prohibition is fully internalized: do not burden May. Do not let May see the bad thing. Do not let May know you are afraid, hurt, in trouble, in love, in danger.

This is the **invalidating environment** in the precise Linehan/Chapman sense, *but with a critical modification*: the invalidation here is not hostile (May is not cold, not punitive, not dismissive). The invalidation is *protective*. May would never have told him to suppress his feelings; he suppressed them because expressing them would have hurt the person he most loved. This is a more insidious variant than the classical model, because the subject cannot resent the source — he can only resent himself for feeling things that, if voiced, would damage her. Across canon, the subject's most reliable internal monologue when distressed is some variation of *I can't tell May*. (Cited verbatim or in paraphrase: *ASM* #18, #50, #100, #200, #400, *J. Michael Straczynski* run #30s, throughout Slott.)

The consequence is the subject's lifelong inability to ask for help, to disclose suffering, to allow himself to be seen weak. The mask is, in this sense, prefigured before it is woven.

## 1.6 EARLY CHILDHOOD BEHAVIORAL PATTERNS

By approximately age six to eight, the file's reconstruction (drawing from *Untold Tales* #1, #16, #25; *ASM* #-1; Mark Waid's *Marvels* #4 sidelong depictions; and the Bendis *Ultimate* origin reworking #1–7 as parallel construction) shows the following stabilized patterns:

- **Solitary play, heavily mechanical.** Disassembly and reassembly of household objects (the toaster incident referenced in *Untold Tales*; the radio he rebuilt at nine). The subject's hands learned fine-motor competence early and he sought tactile-mechanical engagement as a primary mode of self-soothing.
- **Reading omnivory.** Library cards, science magazines (*Popular Mechanics*, *Scientific American*), Aunt May's *Reader's Digest* read for the human-interest stories. He read at adult level by age ten, and this is the consistent baseline depiction.
- **Hyperverbal in the home, mute outside it.** The split is canonically established — talkative with Ben and May at dinner, near-silent at school. The same boy who would not raise his hand in class would, at the kitchen table, hold forth on the orbital mechanics of Sputnik or the chemistry of photographic developer.
- **Conflict avoidance bordering on the somatic.** Stomach upset before school days are referenced obliquely in *Untold Tales*; the somatic conversion of anxiety is an early-installed pattern visible thereafter in his adult life (the headaches Slott depicts; the persistent low-grade nausea before high-risk encounters that DeMatteis names).
- **An intense, premature moral seriousness.** Not piety — the family was not strongly religious, though May has been depicted as observant in moderate Protestant register — but an unusually early and unusually rigid sense of *fairness*, of what people owe each other. The subject is depicted at age eight returning a wallet to a stranger (*Untold Tales*); refusing to participate in the petty cruelties of his peer cohort; carrying a sense of obligation toward smaller children that the cohort found odd.

## 1.7 SCHOOLING — MIDTOWN AND PRECEDING

The subject attended P.S. 174 (Forest Hills) for elementary years per canonical reference, then matriculated to Midtown High School in Queens by approximately age thirteen. The educational trajectory is one of accelerating academic distinction paralleled by accelerating social exclusion.

**Academic.** Top of the class in science from the first year of middle school. Identified by the Midtown chemistry and physics faculty (Mr. Warren, later disastrously to become the Jackal, taught chemistry; Mr. Petty per Lee/Ditko ran physics) as exceptional. Won the science fair (referenced in *AF* #15 backstory) prior to the spider bite. Was invited to the radioactivity demonstration at the General Techtronics Labs facility on the basis of this distinction — that is, **his intelligence is what placed him in the room with the spider**. The causal chain runs through the trait that was already, by that age, his primary source of self-worth.

**Social.** The file's most consequential thread. The Midtown environment is, on the evidence, not merely indifferent but actively cruel. The Lee/Ditko panels of *AF* #15 are unambiguous: the boy is the standing object of group derision. **Flash Thompson**, the football-team archetype, is the principal antagonist; the canonical taunt "Puny Parker" is established in *AF* #15 and reprised across decades. **Liz Allan**, the in-group female lead, treats him with a mixture of pity and casual exclusion that is, developmentally, often more damaging than overt hostility — the message *you are not the kind of person to whom things are offered* lands harder than open mockery.

The exclusion is not occasional; it is depicted as the chronic baseline. He eats lunch alone. He is not invited. He is consistently the object reference for what one does not want to be. Importantly, *the household cannot hear about it* — to tell May would worry her; to tell Ben would shame himself. The boy comes home, goes to the basement, builds something.

This is, in clinical reconstruction, the period in which the **bifurcated self** is laid down. Not the Spider-Man/Peter split — that comes later — but its precursor: the **private competent self** (basement, books, labs, the small world he controls) and the **public defective self** (hallways, gym class, the cafeteria). The Spider-Man identity, when it arrives, slots into a slot already cut for it. It does not invent the bifurcation; it inherits it.

## 1.8 THE PRE-BITE PEER ECOLOGY

Friends, in the documented record, are essentially absent. The subject had acquaintances of mutual scientific interest; he did not, before the bite, have a sustained peer friendship. The deprivation here is severe and is the substrate for the rapid, intense, almost unguarded affection he later shows to anyone — Johnny Storm, Harry Osborn, Hobie Brown, Miles Morales — who treats him as an equal. He has the affect-hunger of someone who went without.

The exception worth noting is the early proto-bond with **Sally Avril** and the slight, awkward connection with **Jason Ionello** (developed in *Untold Tales of Spider-Man*); these are partial and ambivalent. Sally's later death (also *Untold Tales*) becomes one of the first overlay losses on the Ben template — a peer he failed to protect.

## 1.9 BODY AND PRESENTATION, PRE-BITE

Slight build, glasses (the canonical horn-rim, *AF* #15), characteristic stoop in the shoulders, eyes-down gait, hands in pockets. The body itself was a site of failure for him — picked last in gym, unable to make the throw, unable to run the lap. The subsequent overcorrection — the post-bite somatic transformation — is, in the clinical reconstruction, *received by him as the long-delayed correction of a body that had been wrong*. He does not, in early post-bite panels, treat the new body as alien; he treats it as the body he should have had. This is diagnostically relevant: it means the alteration does not destabilize an established somatic identity, because there was no positively-cathected somatic identity to destabilize.

## 1.10 RITUALS AND MICRO-HABITS OBSERVABLE BY AGE FOURTEEN

Reconstructed from the cumulative incidental record:

- **Dinner at the kitchen table, nightly, the same three chairs.** May cooked. Ben asked about school. The boy gave the curated, May-protective version. This ritual is, in the deepest sense, the matrix of his moral life.
- **Wheatcakes on Sunday morning** (May's specialty, referenced repeatedly from *ASM* #18 forward). The smell of them is, decades later, the single olfactory cue most reliably associated in his internal monologue with safety.
- **The basement after school, hours unaccounted for** to the household, which trusted him absolutely.
- **The walk home from school**, deliberately routed to avoid the streets where the bully cohort congregated. The subject was, before he was Spider-Man, **already an expert in route planning for threat avoidance** — a competence he would later weaponize.
- **A precocious, slightly embarrassed kindness toward animals and smaller children**, observed by neighbors and referenced in *Untold Tales*' civilian-perspective issues.

## 1.11 THE UNCLE BEN TEMPLATE — PRE-INSTALLATION

It is essential to the file's clinical accuracy to note that the **Uncle Ben template did not begin with Uncle Ben's death**. The death actualized and named a pattern that the prior fourteen years had already laid down. The subject had already learned: love is precarious (parents gone, May breakable); my honest feelings endanger those I love (the May-fragility chain); the people who matter most to me can vanish without warning (the parents); I am, in the world outside the home, the wrong kind of person (Midtown). The murder of Ben Parker, when it comes, is the moment at which a structure already built receives its first major load — and holds, by being reorganized around guilt.

The boy who walked into the General Techtronics demonstration was, on the evidence:

- Intellectually gifted to a degree that isolated him further.
- Socially excluded to a degree that had become chronic and identity-organizing.
- Emotionally suppressed in service of a fragile primary caregiver.
- Morally serious to a degree well beyond his cohort.
- Already in possession of a private/public self-split.
- Already, in micro, **a custodian** — the boy who watched out for May's health, who managed Ben's worries, who did not make trouble, who came home on time.

He was, in other words, **pre-formed for the role**. The bite did not create a hero; it gave a custodian the somatic toolkit to do at scale what he had already been doing at the kitchen table since he was eight.

What he was not yet, and what the next chronological section must address, is the boy who learned that custody is not enough — that watching out for the ones you love can fail catastrophically, and that the failure will not be repaired, only carried.

— END CHRONOLOGY I —


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

*Subject: PARKER, Peter Benjamin. Period under review: approx. age 13 through approx. age 19. Forest Hills, Queens → Midtown High School → Empire State University. The window in which the somatic transformation occurred, the foundational moral wound was sustained, the operational identity was constructed, and the load-bearing relationship templates were set. All inferences derived from the behavioral record; cross-referenced to Amazing Fantasy #15, Amazing Spider-Man #1–100, the Lee/Ditko and Lee/Romita Sr. canon, and corroborating later reconstructions (Conway, DeMatteis, Straczynski, Slott).*

---

## 1. PRE-BITE BASELINE: MIDTOWN HIGH, AGES 13–15

The subject entered adolescence already shaped by the variables laid out in Chronology I — early parental absence rationalized as void, a warm but anxious caregiver dyad, an implicit prohibition on burdening Aunt May with affect. Midtown High School activated the second formative axis: the chronic, durational experience of social rejection by a peer environment.

**Routine of the period.** The behavioral record across AF #15 and the early Lee/Ditko strips supports a tightly bounded daily perimeter: the Parker house on a residential block of Forest Hills; the bus to Midtown; the school's chemistry and physics labs (where he had unsupervised after-hours access by sophomore year, a privilege extended by faculty who had identified his aptitude); the public library; the basement at home, which functioned as workshop, retreat, and de facto bedroom-of-the-mind. Movement between these nodes was solitary. The subject did not loiter in hallways, did not eat lunch in groups, did not attend dances, football games, or after-school social functions. He carried books in front of his chest in a defensive posture visible in the Ditko panels — a small but consistent somatic tell of bracing.

**Peer environment.** Flash Thompson's bullying is the documented exemplar but the behavioral pattern is broader: Peter was not merely ignored, he was *marked* — singled out as the local lowest-status target, the boy whose name ("Puny Parker") was a school-wide social shorthand. Liz Allan's circle excluded him with a particular cruelty (the casual rejection at the science exhibit in AF #15, in which the same students who mocked him as a bookworm refused to attend a public lecture by a leading nuclear scientist). This is the invalidating environment in its purest adolescent form: the subject's strengths were treated as defects, his interests as evidence of unfitness, his attempts at participation as material for further mockery.

**Compensatory pattern, pre-powers.** Already visible: (a) hyper-intellectualism as both genuine vocation and identity-defense — by age 15 he was reading at graduate level in chemistry, electrical engineering, and applied physics, with particular fluency in polymer chemistry and adhesive mechanics (the substrate that would later produce the web fluid); (b) performative indifference — the "who needs them" posture, audible in his internal narration across the Ditko run, which is a textbook reaction formation; (c) basement retreat — the workshop functioned as a regulated environment in which mastery was possible and rejection structurally impossible; (d) careful management of Aunt May's anxiety — the subject had, by age 15, learned to filter his school day into edited bulletins, omitting the bullying entirely. This last item is the critical datum: he was already running a two-track self-presentation system years before the mask, performing competence and contentment for May while privately metabolizing humiliation alone. The bifurcated self-structure that would later organize the Spider-Man / Peter Parker split was rehearsed in this period.

**Affect at baseline.** Subdued, watchful, sardonic in private monologue, externally compliant. The capacity for the sharp verbal cut existed pre-bite — the internal narration is full of it — but he did not deploy it socially. The quip was, at this stage, a defense held in reserve, used only against threats he could not afford to engage directly. The unmasking of this private wit into public verbal output is one of the documented downstream effects of the role assumption.

---

## 2. THE INCITING EVENT: A 48-HOUR SEQUENCE

The behavioral pivot of the subject's entire subsequent life is compressed into approximately two days. The granular sequence, reconstructed from AF #15 and corroborated across later retellings:

**Hour 0 — the science demonstration.** A public exhibition at a Manhattan research facility on the handling of radioactive waste. The subject attended alone, having been refused company by the Liz Allan group. During the demonstration, a common house spider passed through the particle beam and, in the moments before its death, descended on its dragline and bit the subject on the dorsum of the right hand. The behavioral record indicates the bite was painful enough to register but not alarming; the subject left the demonstration on foot, nauseated, with somatic symptoms (vertigo, altered proprioception) that he initially attributed to the unfamiliar laboratory environment. He walked, rather than took the bus — the first instance of the now-lifelong pattern of seeking motion as affect regulation.

**Hours 1–6 — emergent transformation.** The somatic conversion occurred in transit and at home. By the time he reached the residential blocks of Forest Hills, the strength augmentation was sufficient that he crushed a steel pipe in a reflexive grab and adhered to a brick wall by accident while avoiding a passing car. The behavioral signal here, even at the moment of unprecedented neurological reorganization, is *concealment*: he did not return home and tell May and Ben. He retreated, instead, into the same private channel into which he had been routing every previous unprocessed event of his adolescence. This is the critical pre-figuration: the subject's first response to a life-altering datum was to hide it from his attachment figures and metabolize it in private. The pattern that would later produce sixty years of secret-keeping was already operational on day one.

**Hours 6–24 — the wrestling circuit.** Within hours of confirming the powers, the subject's first deployment of them was monetary. The behavioral inference here is essential and frequently underweighted: he did not consider heroism, he did not consider disclosure, he considered *the rent*. The Parker household's financial precarity had been a constant low-grade pressure throughout his adolescence — Ben's irregular employment, May's medical expenses, the absence of margin — and the subject's first instinct upon acquiring power was to convert it into household stability. He fabricated a mask (initially crude, a cloth pullover) specifically to protect his identity from peers who would mock the spectacle, entered an amateur wrestling exhibition, defeated the headlining adult challenger, and collected the prize money. This first costume was a fame-shield against the high school social environment, not yet a secret-identity apparatus in the mature sense — but the function bled into the latter almost immediately.

**Hours 24–36 — the television offer and the design of the suit.** The wrestling win produced media attention. A television agent offered an appearance. The subject upgraded the costume — and the granular detail of this upgrade is diagnostically interesting: working in the basement workshop, he designed not just a costume but the **web-shooters** and the **web fluid** as integrated subsystems, in a span of hours, from existing notes on adhesive polymers he had been developing as a school project. The cognitive output of this period is staggering — a working high-tensile shear-thinning polymer with controlled-degradation curing, a mechanical wrist-mounted spinneret with a trigger geometry that would not fire from incidental palm pressure, and a full visual identity — and it was produced in a fugue of focused work that is itself a behavioral marker. Under conditions of maximum personal upheaval, the subject's stress response was to *build*. The lab as regulated environment, observed in the pre-bite period, here received its mature function: the workshop is the place where unbearable affect is converted into competent output. This pattern is durable across the next six decades.

**Hour 36 — the corridor.** The pivotal moment. Following the television studio appearance, a fleeing thief ran past the subject in a hallway. A security guard called for him to stop the man. The subject did not. The behavioral content of this non-action is the entire foundation of the file. He was, by his own internal narration, *exhausted* by the prior 36 hours of social punishment — the school's contempt, the wrestling promoter's contempt, the implicit message that the world owed him nothing — and his refusal was a small, almost petty assertion of reciprocal indifference. "Not my problem." It is critical to note that this was not malice. It was a teenager's exhausted shrug, the kind of micro-failure of civic engagement that millions of adolescents commit daily without consequence.

**Hour 48 — the discovery.** The subject returned home to find Aunt May in shock and Uncle Ben dead — shot during a home invasion by a fleeing burglar. The subject, then in costume, pursued. He cornered the killer at the Acme Warehouse. He recognized the man's face. It was the same thief he had refused to stop in the studio corridor approximately twelve hours earlier.

The collapse this datum produced in the subject's interior is the single most consequential psychological event in the file. The guilt did not attach to a thing he did. It attached to a thing he *failed to do*. There is no clean act of atonement available for an omission, because the omission is not undoable — it can only be retroactively counterbalanced by an infinite series of future non-omissions. This is the etiologic template for the lifelong compulsion: every subsequent harm in the world that he could have prevented becomes, structurally, the same harm as Ben's death. The boundary between "harms I caused" and "harms I failed to prevent" was dissolved in this moment and has never been re-established.

The "with great power, there must also come great responsibility" formulation — attributed in the Lee/Ditko canon to a closing caption box, later rendered as a saying of Ben's — is, clinically, the rationalization scaffolding the subject erected within hours over an otherwise unsurvivable wound. It is also, importantly, *load-bearing*: the principle is genuine, the moral commitment is real, and the resulting conduct is durably ethical. The pathological origin does not invalidate the salutary effect. But the file should not mistake the scaffolding for the wound it covers.

---

## 3. THE FIRST SIX MONTHS: ROLE CONSTRUCTION (ASM #1–10)

The period immediately following Ben's death is the construction phase of the operational identity. The subject made a series of choices in rapid sequence that established the parameters of the role for the next sixty years.

**Choice 1: continuation of concealment from May.** With Ben dead and May now a widow with no household income, the rational disclosure would have been to tell her — explain the powers, explain the financial possibilities, explain the guilt, and accept her response. He did not. He doubled down on concealment, and the rationale he constructed (her fragility, her grief, her heart) is the rationale he has continued to deploy for six decades. This is the moment the secret-keeping became structural rather than situational.

**Choice 2: monetization of the role via photography rather than via combat.** The subject's solution to the household financial crisis was characteristically oblique: rather than continue wrestling (lucrative, public, available) or hire out the powers commercially, he conceived of selling photographs of Spider-Man to the *Daily Bugle*, taken by himself via remotely triggered cameras. This is diagnostically rich. He chose the option that (a) maintained the secret-identity architecture, (b) routed the income through his intellectual rather than physical capacity, (c) preserved deniability, and (d) placed him in a structural conflict-of-interest he would never resolve — selling images of himself to the publication most committed to his defamation. The last point is critical: the subject's first sustained adult professional relationship was with a man (J. Jonah Jameson) who publicly hated him. The subject did not just tolerate this — he organized his livelihood around it. The behavioral inference is that he was, even in the first months, already arranging external conditions that mirrored his internal self-assessment. Jameson's contempt was congruent with his guilt; the daily transaction at the Bugle was, in effect, the daily ritual of receiving the punishment the world owed him for the corridor.

**Choice 3: the no-kill commitment.** Not articulated formally in the early issues but enacted from the first combat engagement (the Chameleon, ASM #1). The subject — possessing strength sufficient to easily kill any human-baseline opponent — calibrated his combat output from the outset toward incapacitation rather than lethality. The clinical reading here is not philosophical-deontological but motivated: the subject had already, in his own internal account, killed Uncle Ben by omission. A second death by his hand would constitute confirmation of an identity he could not survive carrying. The no-kill rule is, in this period and through the present, a structural defense of the self-concept as much as a moral commitment.

**Choice 4: the public posture.** The subject deliberately constructed the Spider-Man surface persona — boisterous, mocking, verbally aggressive in combat — as the explicit inverse of the Peter Parker surface. This was not unconscious; the Lee/Ditko run contains internal narration in which the subject reflects on the deliberate quality of the performance. The private wit, suppressed throughout adolescence by social cost, was released through the mask into public verbal output. The quip's emergence is therefore precisely datable: it begins in this six-month construction phase as a deliberate identity-differentiation strategy, and only later (over the following two to three years) becomes the autonomic affect-regulation system it currently is.

---

## 4. EARLY ROGUES AND THE STABILIZATION OF THE COMBAT IDENTITY (ASM #1–38)

The Lee/Ditko run from ASM #1 through #38 represents the period in which the subject confronted, in sequence, a series of antagonists who tested and shaped specific facets of the operational identity.

- **Chameleon (ASM #1).** Tested identity itself — established that the secret-identity apparatus would be repeatedly targeted, and that vigilance over it was permanent.
- **Vulture (ASM #2).** Tested aerial combat — established the somatic confidence in three-dimensional movement.
- **Doctor Octopus (ASM #3, #11–12, #31–33).** The defining adversary of the period. The first opponent who defeated him decisively (ASM #3), producing a depressive crisis the subject resolved by recourse to the lab — engineering a tactical solution overnight and re-engaging successfully. This pattern (defeat → withdrawal to workshop → engineered counter → return) became the durable template for the subject's response to any threat exceeding his immediate envelope. The Master Planner sub-arc (ASM #31–33) is the canonical image of the period.
- **Sandman, Mysterio, Kraven, Scorpion, Electro, Lizard, Green Goblin.** The accumulating rogues' gallery — but more importantly, the accumulating *survivors* of his restraint. Each villain he defeated and did not kill became a future re-engagement, and the cumulative weight of this — the knowledge that his moral commitment guaranteed his future suffering — is itself a stressor he absorbed without revising the commitment.

**The Master Planner arc (ASM #31–33).** This must be examined in its own right. May, dying. A serum required. Doctor Octopus's underwater base. The subject, pinned under collapsed machinery in a flooding chamber, alone, internal narration cycling through Ben and through the impossibility of failure. The image of the subject lifting the machinery — drawn by Ditko in three pages of escalating effort — is the visual codification of the subject's interior across the next six decades: crushed, alone, refusing collapse because someone else will die if he does. This is not the subject discovering his strength; this is the subject discovering the *condition under which his strength is available*, which is the condition of another's survival being staked on it. The behavioral inference matters: the subject does not operate at his full envelope for himself. He operates at full envelope only when an attachment figure is the stake. This calibration has held across the entire subsequent file.

---

## 5. THE FIRST RELATIONSHIPS

The relational templates of the formation period are as durable as the combat templates.

**Aunt May.** The relationship was reorganized by Ben's death into a structure that has not since changed: subject as protector, May as the fragile center, communication carefully edited to omit any content that might burden her. The subject's failure to disclose the costumed life is, in his own framing, an act of love — and it is — but it is also the longest-running instance of the secret-keeping pattern, and it has corroded the relationship in ways the subject does not permit himself to recognize. May has had, across the canon, multiple periods of suspicion, multiple near-disclosures, and (in the post-OMD and Straczynski reconstructions) periods of full disclosure followed by amnestic restoration. The relationship's center of gravity is the unspoken thing.

**Betty Brant (ASM #4 onward).** First romantic attachment. The pattern was set immediately: rapid intensity, secret-keeping, repeated disappearances rationalized as photography assignments, the eventual collapse of the relationship under the accumulated weight of the unexplained absences and Betty's parallel exposure to costumed violence (her brother Bennett's death). The diagnostic content here is the *first iteration* of what became the lifelong relational signature: the subject pursues, secures, then sabotages through the very obligation that defines the costumed life. Betty did not leave because she stopped loving him. She left because she could not be in a relationship with a person whose absences had no explanation she was permitted to receive.

**Liz Allan.** The reversal of the high-school dynamic. By the end of the Midtown High period, Liz had reassessed the subject and pursued affection. He could not metabolize the reassessment. The behavioral record shows him deflecting, joking, retreating — partly because his attention had moved to Betty, partly because Liz's interest required him to revise the foundational self-concept of unlovability, which is a revision he has never fully been able to accept.

**Flash Thompson.** The bullying did not stop at graduation — it converted. Flash, who tormented Peter Parker, became one of Spider-Man's most ardent public defenders. The subject was therefore, from approximately age 16 onward, in the ongoing structurally absurd position of being despised by his bully in one identity and idolized by the same bully in the other. The clinical reading: this is the formative external confirmation of the bifurcated self-system. The world genuinely treated his two selves as different people, and the world's treatment validated the internal split.

**Harry Osborn (entering ASM #31 at ESU).** The first true peer friendship of the subject's life. Harry's father is Norman Osborn (eventual Green Goblin, eventual murderer of Gwen Stacy) — a structural fact the subject did not yet know but which would, in retrospect, become one of the great ironies of the entire file. The friendship was genuine, was sustained through Harry's substance crisis (ASM #96–98), and gave the subject his first sustained experience of male peer attachment since Ben. The friendship's eventual catastrophic rupture (post-Gwen) is one of the unhealed losses of the broader file, but the formation-period friendship is real and is the subject's first evidence that he is capable of being chosen by a peer.

**Gwen Stacy (entering ASM #31).** The relationship that defined the latter half of the formation period and whose loss closed it. Gwen — brilliant, science-fluent, capable of meeting the subject intellectually in a way no prior partner had — became the first attachment in which the subject's Peter-identity rather than his Spider-identity was the engaged surface. The relationship's collapse (covered in Chronology III) is the closing event of formation and the opening event of the mature phase. But within the formation window proper, the relationship's most significant feature is that it was the first time the subject considered the possibility of integration — a life in which the two selves might be unified through a partner who knew him fully. The fact that he never quite told her — the fact that the secret-keeping pattern held even against the most plausible candidate for disclosure of his life — is the formation period's clearest demonstration that the pattern was, by then, no longer a choice but a structure.

**Captain George Stacy.** Gwen's father. Police captain. The subject's first adult male figure since Ben, and the only one who — quietly, never explicitly — identified the subject as Spider-Man and accepted him in both identities. Stacy's eventual death (ASM #90, technically just outside the formation window but conceptually inside it) was the subject's first re-encounter with the Uncle Ben template at the level of an adult attachment. Stacy died saving a child during a fight between Spider-Man and Doctor Octopus, and his last words to the subject were instructions about Gwen. The subject metabolized this loss by adding it to the ledger he was already carrying, not by processing it; this is the moment the ledger became permanent rather than provisional.

---

## 6. ESU AND THE BROADENING OF THE OPERATIONAL ENVELOPE

Empire State University admission (full scholarship, sciences, ASM #31 onward) was the formation period's institutional bridge into adulthood. The subject's behavioral pattern at ESU mirrored his Midtown pattern with one modification: the peer environment was now adult, was now sorted by aptitude rather than by social hierarchy, and was now genuinely receptive to him. He was, for the first time, in a setting where his intellectual capacity was a status asset rather than a target. He did not, however, recalibrate his self-presentation to match. The internal narration across the Lee/Romita run continues to read him as the outsider even as the external evidence had shifted. This is the durable lag-error in his self-perception: external reality updates; internal self-concept does not.

**Workload.** By late formation period (ASM #50–60) the subject was carrying a full undergraduate science load, the Bugle photography work, the household responsibilities, the costumed activity (then averaging multiple engagements per week), and the relationship with Gwen. The behavioral record indicates he was, even then, operating at approximately 2–4 hours of sleep per night. The chronic sleep deprivation that has defined the rest of the file began here. The metabolic implications (combined with the enhanced metabolism's elevated caloric demand) produced the wiry, depleted somatic profile visible across the Romita Sr. art and consistent thereafter.

**Public posture.** Spider-Man, by the end of the formation period, was a known and ambivalent New York fixture — alternately framed as vigilante and as hero in the city's media, beloved by certain neighborhoods (working-class, immigrant, outer-borough) and reviled by the Bugle. The subject had developed, by this point, the now-characteristic patrol patterns: a preferred set of swing lines across midtown and lower Manhattan, with extensions into Queens for proximity to home and into Brooklyn for the bridges. The geographic envelope of the costumed life was set in this period and has remained substantially stable.

---

## 7. THE FORMATION PERIOD AS A STRUCTURE

What was constructed in the approximately six-year window from the bite to the end of the early ESU years can be summarized as a single load-bearing architecture:

A bifurcated self, validated externally by a world that treated the two identities as different people. A no-kill rule held against escalating tests, motivated by a private need rather than a public philosophy. A relational pattern of intense pursuit and unannounced rupture, rationalized as duty but functioning as distance regulation. A secret-keeping protocol so total that it had survived even Gwen and would survive everything thereafter. A workshop-as-regulator, in which un


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Covering the long middle: from the consolidation of adult identity through the marriage years, the great public ruptures, the body-theft, and the slow return. The arc in which the patterns set down in Forest Hills and on the Brooklyn (Marvel-canon: George Washington) Bridge become load-bearing structures of an adult life.*

---

## 1. The Consolidation Phase — Post-Gwen to Pre-Marriage (ASM #122 onward, Wein/Wolfman/Stern eras)

The middle period opens in the wake of Gwen Stacy's death and the immediate retaliation against Norman Osborn (ASM #122). The behavioral record from this point through the late Stern run (#224 or thereabouts) shows a subject reorganizing around a new equilibrium: he has now lost two attachment figures inside his own attempts at protection, and the file shows the first sustained adult version of the bifurcated self that the workup identifies as the engine of the Parker Luck.

Granular markers of this phase, traceable across panels and writers:

- **Residence instability.** He cycles through the Chelsea apartment with Harry Osborn (a relationship the file should flag as one of the few sustained male peer attachments of his life — and one he loses three times: to Harry's addiction, to Harry's Goblin breakdowns, and finally to Harry's death in *Spectacular* #200). After Harry, he lives briefly with Flash Thompson — an inversion of the Midtown High dynamic that the subject never overtly comments on but which a file would note as a self-administered exposure: he chose to share quarters with his childhood scapegoater, and the relationship became one of his most durable.
- **Income pattern crystallizes.** Freelance photography for the *Bugle* becomes the permanent structural arrangement: piecework, irregular, with the man who hates his other self as paymaster. The file should mark this as the first long-running self-sabotage architecture of his adult life — he could have taken any number of stable lab positions (Curt Connors offered; Reed Richards offered repeatedly; Empire State University would have hired him in a heartbeat) and chose the configuration that maximized financial precarity and identity friction. The pattern is consistent with the workup's note that he cannot allow stable success.
- **The Mary Jane reorientation.** After Gwen, MJ is the only person in his social field who knew Gwen, knew Harry, knew Norman, and (it later emerges, ASM #257) had known his secret since the night of Ben's death. The subject's gravitation toward her over this decade is not romantic accident; it is the only relational configuration his system permits. She is pre-disclosed. The file should mark the night she walks away from him on the doorstep (ASM #122 final panel) as one of the two or three most reorganizing micro-events in the entire chronology: she stayed when she could have left, and he never forgot it.
- **The Black Cat interlude (ASM #194 onward).** Felicia Hardy is the counter-test. She loves Spider-Man and is bored by Peter. The relationship runs for years and collapses precisely on the disclosure axis — when he insists on being loved as Peter, she cannot, and the relationship implodes. The file should note that he kept returning to her for years afterward as a non-domestic outlet; she occupies the operational slot of "the woman who knows the mask and not the man," which his system permits as a release valve from the pursuit-of-total-disclosure pressure he otherwise lives under.
- **First sustained Avengers/team work.** He floats in and out of the Fantastic Four's orbit, the Defenders, and eventually the Avengers reserve. The pattern is: he accepts the invitation, attends two or three meetings, vanishes mid-crisis, returns with apology. He cannot tolerate being institutionalized. The file should mark this as continuous with the Bugle pattern — he requires arrangements he can quit at any moment.

The Stern run delivers the **Hobgoblin** arc (ASM #238 onward), in which the unmasking-from-the-outside threat becomes a sustained operating condition for the first time. Behavioral signature in this period: increased night-patrol hours, decreased lab time, a documented shift in his quip register toward sharper and more clipped delivery under Stern's pen — the humor becomes more controlled, less manic, which is the file's first marker of the subject having matured the affect-regulation strategy into something approaching a craft.

The **death of Jean DeWolff** (*Spectacular* #107–110, Peter David, 1986) belongs in this phase as a discrete trauma deposit. A police captain — an authority figure who had actually accepted him — murdered, and Peter beats the Sin-Eater nearly to death before Daredevil stops him. The file should mark this as the second on-record loss of behavioral control after the post-Gwen Osborn beating, and the first time he is named by an ally as having approached the line he claims not to cross. He does not metabolize this either; he files it.

---

## 2. The Marriage Years — Stability as Stressor (ASM Annual #21, 1987 → "Brand New Day," 2007)

The marriage is the longest single behavioral experiment in the file: twenty real-world years of forced cohabitation with a partner who knew the secret in advance. The clinical interest is in observing what the subject does when his stated organizing wish — to be loved with full disclosure — is granted.

The answer is that he begins to construct *new* secrets.

Granular pattern markers:

- **Withholding of mission severity.** Across the Michelinie/McFarlane and Larsen runs (ASM #298 onward), the subject systematically underreports injury to MJ. He returns home with cracked ribs and says it was a quiet night. The file should mark this as the first re-emergence of the May-fragility template inside the marriage: he has cast MJ in the structural role of the person who must not be burdened, even as she explicitly demands the opposite.
- **The first symbiote contact (ASM #252, the Secret Wars black suit) and its long aftermath.** The "alien costume" interval is, behaviorally, the file's clearest depiction of dissociative drift in the subject. He sleeps and wakes elsewhere; he patrols longer; the quip recedes; MJ identifies the change before he does (ASM #258 — her terror at the suit is the diagnostic moment). The separation from the suit (and its passage to Eddie Brock) installs Venom as the externalized double — the file should mark this as the third literalization, after the original clone and the late-Stern Hobgoblin-as-friend-or-foe ambiguity, of his internal experience of containing a malign second self.
- **The Kraven burial (*Fearful Symmetry*, DeMatteis, 1987).** Two weeks underground. The file should treat this as the single most psychologically explicit episode in the entire canon. Stripped of motion, voice, and combat — the three affect channels the workup identifies — what surfaces is ideation organized around relief-via-erasure, dream-content saturated with Ben and Gwen, and on emergence a behavioral compression so total that the post-arc Peter is, by MJ's observation, "different for a long time." DeMatteis is uniquely valuable to the file because he refuses to let the subject reset between arcs; the burial is referenced for years afterward in his work as a not-fully-closed wound.
- **The clone saga (1994–96).** Regardless of editorial mismanagement, the in-universe behavioral content is precise: presented with the proposition that he is a copy and Ben Reilly is the original, the subject's first internal response is *relief*. The file should mark this with significance: offered the chance to surrender the identity that has cost him everything, his initial affect is not horror but unburdening. The subsequent re-establishment of his own primacy is reluctant. Ben Reilly's death at Osborn's hands (Peter Parker: Spider-Man #75) re-instantiates the pattern at yet higher resolution: another attachment figure (in this case, literally himself) killed by the same villain who killed Gwen.
- **The loss and return of May (ASM #400, 1995; reversed later).** Marla Jameson's eventual death and the temporary loss of May during this period both produce the depressive collapse the file expects, but the marriage absorbs them — MJ's presence is, across the late nineties, the only documented exogenous regulator capable of shortening his depressive intervals. The file should note this as the strongest single piece of evidence for the workup's contention that secure relational disclosure is genuinely curative for him; the system was working, and he could not let it continue working.
- **MJ's modeling and acting career, the stalker arc, the plane "crash."** When MJ develops an independent life that places her physically out of his protective radius, his anxiety intrudes into the marriage in operationally observable ways: increased web-shadowing of her schedule, jealousy he intellectualizes as concern, and ultimately the period of estrangement that closes the John Byrne *Spider-Man: Chapter One*-era runs. The pattern is consistent with the fearful-avoidant component: he can tolerate her presence and her absence, but he cannot tolerate her *autonomous* presence at a distance, because that configuration most closely resembles the originating loss.

The **Mackie/Byrne reboot, the "Howard Mackie era,"** and the run-up to Straczynski belong in the file as a wilderness interval — editorial chaos, but the behavioral signal recoverable from it is the subject's continued reliance on the marriage as ballast even as the writing destabilizes everything around him.

---

## 3. The Straczynski Reorientation (ASM Vol. 2 #30 onward, 2001–2007)

JMS introduces the totem question — was the spider chosen, or was Peter chosen by the spider? — and Morlun as the totem-hunter. The file should mark this period as the one in which the subject is forced, for the first time, to interrogate the meaning of his own transformation, which the prior thirty years of canon had treated as accidental.

Granular behavioral shifts under JMS:

- **Re-engagement with May as an adult.** ASM Vol. 2 #38, the kitchen scene in which May reveals she has known about Spider-Man for years and confronts him on Ben — this is, in the entire file, the first time the subject is permitted by his author to *speak the guilt aloud* to the person it most concerns, and to be told he is forgiven. The file should mark this as a discrete metabolic event: post-#38, the May relationship operates on different terms, and a measurable softening in his domestic affect is visible across the next two years of issues.
- **The teaching post at Midtown High.** He returns to the building of his scapegoating as a science teacher. The file should mark this as either the most therapeutic single life choice he has made or the most masochistic — and the behavioral record suggests both simultaneously. He is good at it; he loves it; he loses it inside two years, in the pattern.
- **The Avengers tenure (New Avengers, Bendis, 2005 onward) and residence at Stark Tower.** For the first time, the subject accepts both a team and a sponsor. The file should note the dependency vector: Stark provides costume, lab, housing, and surrogate-father presence. The subject's defenses against this are visible — increased quipping at Stark specifically, repeated small refusals — but the broader pattern is that he accepts the arrangement, which is anomalous for him and which sets up the catastrophic withdrawal to follow.
- **Morlun and "The Other."** Clinical death and rebirth. The file should mark the post-Other interval (organic web-shooters, stingers, night-vision) as a somatic intrusion the subject never fully integrates — the abilities are present, then quietly recede from the writing, and his own narration around them is consistently dissociated. Bodies that change without consent are the through-line of his somatic history, and this is one more.

## 4. *Civil War* and the Unmasking — The Catastrophic Disclosure (2006–2007)

The single most destabilizing public event of the middle period. Under Stark's pressure, the subject unmasks on live television (*Civil War* #2). The behavioral record across the subsequent year is precise and ugly:

- **Initial euphoria.** He reports relief — the wall between selves is down. The file should mark this as a known false dawn: subjects whose pathology is organized around a maintained division often experience the moment of collapse as liberation before the actual cost arrives.
- **Defection from the Pro-Registration side.** Triggered by the discovery of Negative Zone Prison 42 — the moral-compromise tripwire identified in the personality workup. The defiance is sudden, total, and irreversible; the file should note the speed of the reversal as diagnostic of the deontological-with-guilt-substrate operating code.
- **The hunt.** May is shot by a Kingpin sniper aimed at Peter (*Back in Black*, ASM #538–545). The unmasking has converted the structural fear of his life — that an attachment figure will die because of him — into a literal causal chain. The file should mark the **Back in Black** interval as the second documented sustained-rage episode of the adult chronology (after Sin-Eater), in which the no-kill rule is held by the thinnest possible margin. He visits Kingpin in prison and beats him without the mask. He does not kill him. The restraint, given the provocation, is the single largest data point in the file for the workup's claim that the prosocial scaffolding is structurally intact.
- **"One More Day."** The subject trades the marriage to Mephisto in exchange for May's life. The file should not litigate the editorial controversy; the behavioral content is unambiguous and entirely consistent with the workup's central pattern. Offered the choice between the relationship that had been curative and the attachment figure whose death would re-instantiate the Ben template, he chooses the template. He gives up the one configuration in which he had been demonstrably whole, because allowing May to die was, for his system, not a choice that could be made. The cost — twenty years of marriage erased from causal history — is exactly the kind of cost the workup predicts he will pay: self for other, totally, with the calculus inverted to obscure that *the marriage was the self*.

The file should mark the post-OMD interval as the longest sustained psychological setback in the chronology. He does not know what he has lost; the texture of his daily affect across the *Brand New Day* run (Slott, Wells, Guggenheim, Gale, 2008 onward) is observably more brittle, the quipping more frantic, the relational pattern reverted to pre-marriage adolescent rhythms (serial brief relationships, none disclosed, all collapsing on the same axis).

## 5. The *Brand New Day* and *Big Time* Intervals (2008–2012)

Operationally a regression to the bachelor configuration, but with the residue of everything prior. Granular markers:

- **Multiple unstable residences** — Aunt May's again, a flop at a Bugle colleague's, eventually the loft.
- **Carlie Cooper** as the post-MJ attempt at a fully-disclosed relationship; the file should mark her as the template's faithful replication and its predictable failure (he keeps the secret too long, she leaves on the exact disclosure-timing axis).
- **The death of Marla Jameson** (ASM #654). Jonah's wife, killed by a Spider-Slayer aimed at Peter. The file should mark the deposition of this loss onto the existing Stacy/DeWolff/Ben/Gwen/Harry/Ben Reilly stack as cumulative load that begins to drive the *Big Time* phase's brief experiment in lethal-force-prevention vows ("no one dies").
- **Horizon Labs.** First adult stable employment in his actual field. The file should mark this as a brief functional improvement and note that he loses it inside two years, in the pattern. While it lasts, the inventive output (cryo-cube webbing, suit upgrades, anti-everything contingency suits) is the highest sustained engineering productivity of his life, which is consistent with the workup's observation that intellectualization is a primary defense — given stable lab access, the defense becomes generative.

## 6. The Body-Theft — *Superior Spider-Man* (Slott, 2012–14)

The file should treat this interval with the gravity of a sustained dissociative violation, because that is what it operationally was.

Otto Octavius performs a consciousness swap. Peter dies in Otto's failing body; his own body is occupied by Octavius, who operates as Spider-Man for over a year of in-universe time. A suppressed echo of Peter persists at the margins of the body's cognition and is eventually able to reassert control.

Behavioral content recoverable from the post-Superior chronology:
