**Evolution.** Early period: pure adversary. Middle period (post-May-engagement): adversarial-with-personal-violation; Octavius's pursuit of May is one of the few villain moves the subject treats as unforgivable in the same register as Osborn's. Late period (post-Superior): something genuinely unprecedented — the man who lived inside his skin, ran his life, slept with his girlfriend (Anna Maria), and discovered, by occupying the role, that being him was *harder than it looked*. Octavius emerges from the body-theft with measurable respect for the subject, and the subject emerges with measurable contamination: Anna Maria's existence, the doctorate Octavius half-completed in his name, the relationships Octavius repaired or ruined. The post-Superior dynamic is the closest thing in the file to a *peer* relationship the subject has with anyone, because Octavius is the only person alive who has experienced the full interior load of being him.

**Trust/Safety.** Conditional and unstable. The subject will work with him in extremis (Spencer-era cooperation) and will not turn his back. Octavius's affect toward Peter has shifted from hatred to a complicated possessive admiration; the subject finds this *more* disturbing than the hatred.

**Failure mode.** Identity destabilization. Every Octavius encounter post-2014 reactivates the body-theft trauma; the subject's intrusive re-experiencing is most documented in this relationship.

**Leverage.** Octavius holds the most dangerous possible intelligence: lived experience of the subject's body, mind, finances, passwords, romantic patterns, and tactical habits. He is the only adversary who knows the subject *from inside*. He has so far not fully weaponized this, which itself is a datum.

---

### J. Jonah Jameson

**History.** ASM #1 onward; six decades of editorial persecution, public defamation, occasional alliance, eventual knowing-the-secret reconciliation (Slott, Spencer).

**Dynamics.** Not an enemy in the rogue sense — an *adversarial attachment*. Jameson is one of the most important relationships in the subject's life and functions, structurally, as a displaced paternal figure against whom Peter can safely express the anger he cannot direct at Ben (because Ben is dead and sanctified) or May (because May is fragile). The relationship is held together by mutual need: Peter needs Jameson's checks and the daily abrasion that lets him externalize self-contempt; Jameson needs Peter's photographs and, beneath that, the only employee whose moral seriousness matches his own. The hostility is real and the affection is real and they are the same affection.

**Evolution.** Early: pure exploitation, with Jameson genuinely believing the Spider-Menace narrative he sells. Middle: gradual erosion as Jameson is repeatedly saved by, and forced to acknowledge, the subject's conduct (the Marla Jameson arc is the inflection). Late: Jameson discovers the identity, and the discovery — which a different writer might have played as catastrophic — produces, instead, the closest thing to paternal acceptance the subject has had since Ben. Marla's death and Jameson's subsequent breakdown produce a role inversion in which Peter is the steady one.

**Trust/Safety.** Paradoxically high. Jameson's hostility is *predictable*, which in this subject's economy is more trustworthy than most professed loyalty. After the reveal, Jameson has held the secret.

**Failure mode.** Peter under-charges, over-delivers, accepts abuse he would not accept from anyone else — because the abuse is, functionally, the form their love takes, and the subject reads being-yelled-at as being-attended-to.

**Leverage.** Jameson holds the secret now, and the file of his old editorials — the public-record damage to Peter's reputation — remains a structural drag on the subject's civilian life even after the personal reconciliation.

---

### Eddie Brock — Venom

**History.** First emergence, ASM #298–300 (Michelinie/McFarlane); the long enmity through the 1990s; the periodic anti-hero phases; the Cates-era cosmic-symbiote retcons; the late-era detente.

**Dynamics.** The doppelgänger enemy. The symbiote, having lived on Peter, learned the interior shape of him — the rejection-sensitivity, the loneliness, the rage Peter does not let himself feel — and then bonded with a man (Brock) who had been professionally destroyed by association with Peter. Venom is, more than any other rogue, *made of* Peter's rejected material. The black-suit period (Secret Wars I, ASM #252 onward) is the only documented episode in which the subject allowed an external agent to do his affect regulation for him, and the cost was nearly his soul; rejecting the symbiote (Web of Spider-Man #1) was a healthy act with a hidden price tag, because the rejected material did not vanish — it walked away wearing Brock's body.

**Evolution.** Early: existential terror; Venom is the one enemy whose spider-sense the subject cannot read, and the subject's combat doctrine has to be rebuilt around the blind spot. Middle: grudging acknowledgment of Brock's quasi-coherent moral code. Late: tactical alliance, mutual recognition, almost-friendship across writers willing to let it land.

**Trust/Safety.** Low but improving. The subject has learned that Brock can be reasoned with; he has not learned to be comfortable in his presence.

**Failure mode.** The spider-sense blind spot is the literal correlate of the relational blind spot — the subject does not see Venom coming because Venom is, in some sense, *already inside him*.

**Leverage.** Venom holds the identity, the family addresses, and the historical record of how Peter behaves when he stops disciplining himself. The dormant leverage is psychological: any encounter reactivates the shame of the black-suit period, in which Peter discovered he *liked* being unrestrained.

---

### Cletus Kasady — Carnage

**History.** ASM #344 onward; *Maximum Carnage*; the recurrences through Wells and Cates.

**Dynamics.** The enemy who exists to test the no-kill rule and to lose nothing by killing. Kasady is the only adversary the subject has, repeatedly and across writers, *considered* killing — and the refusal is the load-bearing wall of the subject's ethical structure. If he kills Kasady, he becomes a person who kills, which means he becomes a person who could have killed the burglar, which means Ben's death becomes a different kind of fact. The no-kill rule with respect to Carnage is not philosophical; it is autobiographical.

**Trust/Safety.** None. The relationship is pure containment.

**Failure mode.** Moral exhaustion; the subject leaves Carnage encounters more depleted than physical injury accounts for.

**Leverage.** Kasady's leverage is structural rather than informational: every time he kills civilians the subject failed to reach, the Uncle Ben template is re-instantiated. He is a machine for generating the subject's foundational wound on a schedule.

---

### Wilson Fisk — the Kingpin

**History.** ASM #50 onward (Lee/Romita); decades of intermittent confrontation; the Daredevil-borrowing periods; the Spencer "Mayor Fisk" arc.

**Dynamics.** The adult enemy — the one who does not posture, does not monologue, and does not personalize the conflict. Fisk has identified the quip as a tell (this is on record — Fisk has said as much to subordinates) and conducts himself around the subject with the calm of a man who knows he is dealing with a frightened person performing fearlessness. The asymmetry is structural: Fisk has resources, patience, and the ability to harm Peter without ever appearing in person. The subject's tactical response is correspondingly *less* improvisational against Fisk than against any other rogue; Fisk is the adversary who makes Peter plan.

**Trust/Safety.** Zero, and the zero is mutual and professionalized.

**Failure mode.** The subject can outmaneuver Fisk tactically but cannot outlast him institutionally; Fisk's leverage is the city itself.

**Leverage.** Civic infrastructure, legal apparatus, the press the subject cannot afford, and — crucially — the demonstrated willingness to attack family members the subject loves through perfectly legal mechanisms (zoning, employment, housing).

---

### Sergei Kravinoff — Kraven the Hunter

**History.** ASM #15 onward; *Kraven's Last Hunt* (DeMatteis, 1987); the *Grim Hunt* resurrection (2010); subsequent recurrences.

**Dynamics.** The enemy who understood him. Kraven, alone among the rogues, treated Peter as a worthy spiritual adversary and structured his life around the proposition that defeating-and-becoming the subject would resolve his own existential crisis. *Last Hunt* — the burial alive, the impersonation, the release — is the single most psychologically violating episode in the subject's recorded history, and it is the one that surfaces the depressive substrate beneath all defenses, because the burial removed every channel (motion, speech, action) through which the subject regulates affect.

**Trust/Safety.** N/A — Kraven is, in his own register, almost honorable; the subject's response is closer to wary respect than to hatred.

**Failure mode.** The buried-alive episode generated a specific and lasting phobia of immobilization and enclosed spaces; the subject is depicted across post-1987 runs as managing this with deliberate effort.

**Leverage.** Kraven proved that the subject can be psychologically broken; the proof itself is a permanent file in Peter's interior cabinet, available for re-reading whenever a new adversary studies the precedent.

---

### Harry Osborn

**History.** Roommate (ASM #31 onward); the addiction arc (ASM #96–98); first Green Goblin incarnation; death and resurrection across the Mackie/Slott eras.

**Dynamics.** The friend-who-becomes-enemy-who-becomes-friend, on a loop. Harry is the only person in the subject's life who occupies both categories simultaneously and across decades. The friendship is real; the enmity is real; the oscillation traces Harry's mental illness more than Peter's choices, but the subject reads each Harry-relapse as something he failed to prevent — i.e., as another Ben.

**Trust/Safety.** Painfully high during stable periods; painfully low during unstable ones. The subject cannot regulate the oscillation, only endure it.

**Failure mode.** Peter consistently underestimates how much Harry knows and overestimates how much Harry has healed; the asymmetry is driven by Peter's need for the friendship to be intact.

**Leverage.** Harry, like his father, periodically holds the identity. More importantly, Harry holds the *history* — the dorm room, the early failures, the version of Peter that existed before the masks calcified.

---

### Flash Thompson

**History.** Midtown High bully (AF #15 onward); later Spider-Man's most public fan; military service; Agent Venom (Remender, 2011); death and recurrences.

**Dynamics.** Begins as the prototypical invalidating-peer figure and inverts into one of the subject's most durable allies. The inversion is critical: Flash is the proof, in the subject's life, that people can change — which is the proposition the subject must believe in order to keep doing the work, and which his own self-concept does not extend to himself.

**Trust/Safety.** Moderate-to-high; the residual childhood scar tissue never fully resolves but is held with adult awareness on both sides.

**Failure mode.** The subject cannot fully accept Flash's admiration, because accepting it requires accepting that the Spider-Man-self is admirable, which requires revising the bifurcated self-concept.

---

### Quentin Beck — Mysterio

**History.** ASM #13 onward; recurrent across all eras.

**Dynamics.** The enemy who attacks reality testing. The subject, whose entire combat doctrine rests on the spider-sense and on accurate perception, is uniquely vulnerable to an adversary who manipulates perception itself. Mysterio encounters consistently produce, in the subject, a transient hyper-skepticism that he then has to discipline back down to functional levels.

**Failure mode.** Post-Mysterio paranoid spikes; brief periods in which the subject double-checks his sensory data and over-relies on verification rituals.

---

### The Lizard / Curt Connors

**History.** ASM #6 onward.

**Dynamics.** Enemy-as-friend-in-distress. Connors is, in his right mind, a colleague the subject respects; the Lizard is an illness wearing Connors's body. Every confrontation requires Peter to fight a person he wants to save, which is the configuration that most cleanly activates his prosocial-altruism defense and most cleanly demonstrates that the defense *works* — Connors is one of the few rogues the subject has measurably helped, repeatedly.

---

### The minor and structural rogues (composite entry)

**Sandman, Vulture (Toomes), Electro (Dillon), Mysterio (above), Scorpion, Rhino, Shocker, Chameleon, Hobgoblin (Kingsley/Macendale), Morbius, Tombstone, Hammerhead.** Functionally, this roster constitutes the subject's *workplace* — the people he sees on the schedule, against whom his combat doctrine is calibrated, with whom he has the running banter that strangers mistake for the totality of his affect. Several (Toomes, Marko, Dillon) have been periodic objects of the subject's reformation hopes; the failures of those hopes are filed under the same heading as every other failure, which is to say, his fault.

The composite point: the subject *knows* these men. He knows Marko's daughter's name. He knows Dillon's literacy level. He knows Toomes is dying. This knowledge is the texture of his moral life and the substrate of his fatigue.

---

### Morlun and the Inheritors

**History.** JMS-era totem arcs; *Spider-Verse* (Slott).

**Dynamics.** The cosmic predator who established that the subject *can be hunted* — that the universe contains adversaries against whom his usual doctrine is inapplicable. The Morlun fights are the only recorded episodes in which the subject genuinely believed, mid-fight, that he was going to die and stay dead. The Other arc (clinical death, somatic transformation) is one of the file's most significant somatic-violation events.

**Failure mode.** Post-Morlun, the subject's threat-assessment calibration shifts permanently upward; the spider-sense reads differently afterward, and the subject's behavior reflects the change.

---

## II. INTIMATES & LOVERS

### Elizabeth "Betty" Brant

**History.** ASM #4 onward; the first sustained romantic engagement; eventual dissolution; lifelong friendship.

**Dynamics.** The first attempt, and the prototype of the failure mode. Betty was older, working, drawn to Peter for his evident decency and intellect; Peter was drawn to her because she was an adult who treated him as an adult. The relationship dissolved against the secret — every cancelled date, every unexplained injury, every Spider-Man-related absence accumulated into a portrait of an unreliable man, which Betty (rationally) declined to marry. The subject's lifelong residual guilt toward Betty is interpretable as the realization, in retrospect, that *he taught her she was not worth the truth*, which she was.

**Trust/Safety.** Currently high in the friendship register; the romantic register is closed and mourned.

**Failure mode.** Secret-keeping as relational corrosion — the first instance, and the template.

**Leverage.** Betty knows the early Peter — the pre-armored version — and her continued presence in his life functions as a low-grade reminder of who he was before the defenses calcified.

---

### Gwen Stacy

**History.** ASM #31 onward; ASM #121 (death); recurrences across clones, alternates, "Sins Past," and the recurring internal-monologue presence in DeMatteis, Straczynski, and Slott.

**Dynamics.** The unresolved core. Gwen was the first partner the subject loved in the adult register and the first whose loss could not be metabolized. The relationship while she lived was, on the record, *unhappy as often as happy* — Gwen blamed Spider-Man for her father's death, did not know Peter and Spider-Man were the same person, and was therefore in love with one half of a man while hating the other half. The subject lived inside this for years and could not resolve it, because resolution required disclosure and disclosure was unthinkable. Her death short-circuited the resolution forever, freezing the relationship at maximum unresolved-ness — which is the precise condition under which prolonged grief calcifies.

**Trust/Safety.** Posthumously, the relationship has become *more* trusted, not less, because death has removed the possibility of disconfirming the idealization. This is clinically textbook and operationally crippling.

**Failure mode.** Gwen is the standard against which every subsequent partner is silently measured; the subject does not know he is doing this and would deny it if asked.

**Leverage.** Gwen's memory is the single largest piece of leverage in the file, and Osborn holds it. Every "Sins Past"-style retcon, every clone, every alternate-universe Gwen (including the spider-bitten one) is a re-pressing on the same bruise.

---

### Mary Jane Watson

**History.** First appearance, ASM #25 (face obscured); ASM #42 (the famous reveal); on-and-off across the entire Romita/Conway/DeFalco run; marriage, ASM Annual #21 (1987); the "One More Day" dissolution (2007); reconciliation across Slott, Spencer, Wells.

**Dynamics.** The central adult relationship of the subject's life and the only one that has, episodically, *worked*. MJ is selected — and selects herself — precisely because she ident


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

*Subject file fragment. Cross-reference Sections 2 (Medical) and 3 (Psychological); the somatic apparatus and the psychic apparatus are not separable in this subject and the boundary between "power" and "symptom" is, as will be argued, frequently fictive.*

---

## 1. THE ARACHNID ENDOWMENT — MECHANISM AND BASELINE

The bite at the Oscorp/General Techtronics demonstration (Amazing Fantasy #15) introduced a vector — irradiated in the Lee/Ditko original, retconned across decades to genetic, mystical-totemic (JMS, "The Other"), and bio-engineered (Ultimate) variants — that rewrote the subject's somatic baseline at the cellular level. The phenotype is stable across continuities and the operative parameters can be mapped with precision.

**Musculoskeletal strength.** The conservative lifting ceiling, demonstrated repeatedly and consistent across writers from Conway through Slott, sits in the ten-to-fifteen ton range under non-emergency load and ascends to the twenty-five-plus-ton range under maximal adrenal recruitment and life-stakes context. The Master Planner sequence (ASM #33) — collapsed industrial machinery, dying May, the panel of him pushing upward from his knees — established the canonical iconography: he can lift more than his frame should physically transmit, which means the limiting factor is not muscle fiber recruitment but his willingness to keep pushing past the pain signal. Note the operative variable: the ceiling is *psychological*. He lifts what he believes he has to.

**Proportional speed and reflex.** Top sprint speed in the 200-to-300-mph envelope when swinging; pure ground sprint considerably lower but still triple Olympic baseline. Reaction time is sub-conscious — measured in single-digit milliseconds, faster than visual processing, which means he is *acting before he sees*. This has clinical implications addressed below.

**Agility, balance, coordination.** The body has been retuned to operate continuously off-axis. The visual canon — Ditko's contorted crouches, Romita's mid-swing inversions, McFarlane's spider-impossible postures, Bagley's perpetual asymmetric perch — is not stylistic exaggeration; it is accurate depiction of a proprioceptive system that has remapped "neutral" away from human bipedal symmetry. The subject is, at rest, slightly uncomfortable standing upright the way civilians stand.

**Adhesion (the setae).** Microscopic keratinous hair-structures on palmar and plantar surfaces enabling van der Waals adhesion to nearly any surface. Modulable: he can disengage instantly or anchor against multi-G shear. Defeated by surface treatments specifically engineered against it (oil films in several Octopus stratagems; the Doctor Octopus "frictionless polymer" arc), by ice formations under certain conditions, and — pertinently — by the subject's own loss of focus. Adhesion is voluntary, not autonomous; sufficient psychological dissociation has, in canon, caused him to fall (notably post-Gwen, ASM #122–124, and in the post-Kraven recovery arcs).

**The precognitive proprioceptive alert ("spider-sense").** The most diagnostically loaded power. Operates as a sub-cortical threat-detection apparatus calibrated to incoming harm to the subject's person — and, secondarily and less reliably, to harm to those he is psychologically bonded to (a documented extension that has cost him dearly when it failed at the Brooklyn Bridge). Range varies with threat magnitude: small-arms fire registers at meters, sniper threats at hundreds of meters, ordnance at thousands. It does *not* discriminate intention reliably (it has misfired on practical jokes, on Mary Jane sneaking up affectionately, on cameras); it discriminates *trajectory toward the body*. It can be overridden by sufficient psionic interference (Psycho-Man, the Chameleon's neurological gas), suppressed by exhaustion, and notably *silenced* during the Superior occupation and parts of the post-Civil-War period when his own neurochemistry was disrupted.

The clinical reading of spider-sense is unavoidable: the subject has lived his entire adult life inside a never-silent, never-off threat-detection apparatus that fires hundreds of times per day. His nervous system has been reorganized around the assumption that something is, at any given moment, about to hurt him. There is no normative human equivalent for what this does to baseline arousal over four decades of subjective time. (See Section 2; the absence of substance use becomes, in this light, the more remarkable.)

**Healing and biochemical resilience.** Accelerated wound closure, demonstrated repeatedly (broken ribs in twenty-four to seventy-two hours, deep lacerations in days, recoveries from poisoning that would be lethal to baseline humans). Not Wolverine-tier — he can be killed, has been killed, and bleeds visibly in nearly every issue — but sufficient that his medical record (which civilian providers would read as miraculous) shows no scar accumulation commensurate with his injury history.

**Metabolic load.** The price of all of the above. Caloric requirement approximately double baseline, demonstrated in DeFalco and codified by Slott; the protein and lipid burn is severe. Combined with his chronic financial precarity (see Section 7, *Habits & Routines*), this means the subject is *structurally* undernourished a significant fraction of the time. The wiry frame is not a body type; it is a deficit state.

---

## 2. THE FABRICATED EXTENSIONS — INVENTION AS PROSTHETIC

The web-shooters are the single most important datum about the subject's mind that the powers section can articulate, because *he built them*. The spider did not grant projectile silk; a high-school student under sixty hours of grief-induced sleeplessness designed twin pneumatic-mechanical wrist-cartridge launchers and synthesized a polymer that exceeds the tensile strength of steel by mass, dissolves on a one-hour timer, and re-pressurizes from compact CO₂-or-equivalent cartridges worn against the radial pulse.

**Mechanism.** Dual-trigger palm-actuated valve (the tap-the-palm-with-the-ring-and-middle-finger gesture, codified by Ditko and preserved with near-religious continuity by every subsequent artist — a behavioral micro-signature unmistakable to any analyst with footage), variable-aperture nozzle permitting line, net, spray, and blunt-impact configurations. Cartridge capacity sustains roughly ninety minutes of continuous use under typical operational tempo; an empty pair of shooters is the recurring tactical crisis the writers reach for when they want to strip him.

**Polymer.** Adhesive, elastic to roughly the limits of his own arm-strength applied as anchor, dissolves through a programmed scission reaction. He has refined the formula across decades — impact webbing, taser-webbing, stealth-webbing, the "spider-tracer" radio-emitting variants — and the formula itself is, on at least three documented occasions, the McGuffin villains have attempted to steal because no other chemist on Earth has reproduced it.

**Why the synthetic webbing matters psychologically.** The organic-webbing period (post-"Disassembled," JMS) was clinically informative: when the totem-mysticism arc gave him biological web spinnerets, he was visibly diminished as an operator, not because the new power was weaker but because the apparatus he relied on was no longer something he had *made*. He needed the engineering. The web-shooters are the externalization of his intellectualizing defense (Section 3) into the operational stack itself — they are the visible insistence that competence is *built*, not granted. The retreat from organic webs back to mechanical was, for the subject, a restoration of selfhood.

**The Spider-Tracer.** Coin-sized transmitter, tuned to a frequency only he can perceive (retconned across continuities to coordinate with his spider-sense). The signature application is *attaching it during combat without the target noticing*, typically while delivering a quip designed to cover the gesture. This is a tell: he is the rare combatant who does his most strategic work while talking the loudest.

**Costume.** Self-designed, self-sewn (Aunt May's machine, in the Lee/Ditko canon), iterated across decades. The lens-construction has progressed from cosmetic mesh to functional optics (Stark-built iterations in the Civil War period added EM-spectrum overlays; he has reverted to simpler builds whenever Stark proximity becomes politically intolerable). The mask is non-negotiable in his self-system. Removing it in the field is an event so rare it functions as a plot beat.

---

## 3. THE FAR-LATER ACQUISITIONS — POWERS HE WAS GIVEN AND DID NOT KEEP

**Captain Universe ("Cosmic" Spider-Man, ASM #329).** Brief planetary-tier endowment. He returned the power. Worth noting: he is the only documented Captain Universe host who treated the experience as something to *survive* rather than to keep.

**The Other / totem powers (JMS, 2005–2007).** Organic spinnerets, night vision, stingers in the wrist, expanded spider-sense bandwidth. Substantially relinquished or attenuated. See above; the gift was somatically integrated but psychologically rejected.

**Iron Spider armor (Civil War period).** Stark-built nanotech, additional waldo-arms, comms suite. Discarded immediately on his repudiation of registration. The discard was clean and complete — additional confirmation that augmentation he does not himself control is, for this subject, intolerable.

**Superior period (Slott, 2012–14).** Inverse case: the body retained the powers while another consciousness operated it. The relevant datum here is what Octavius *did* with the apparatus that Peter would not — efficiency-maximizing patrol routes, predictive crime modeling, surveillance-network construction, lethal-force escalation — and the corollary inference: Peter's powers have always operated significantly under their theoretical ceiling because *he* has been operating them. The Octavius interregnum is the file's natural-experiment control on the question of how much of "Spider-Man's limits" are the spider and how much is Peter.

The answer, for the record, is: most of it is Peter.

---

## 4. SKILLS — THE ACQUIRED LAYER

**Scientific competence.** Doctoral-level (Slott codifies the eventual PhD; preceding runs establish equivalent functional knowledge across biochemistry, mechanical and electrical engineering, applied physics, and materials science). The competence is genuine, not background-flavor. He has, on documented occasion, out-engineered Reed Richards in narrow domains (adhesion chemistry, certain bio-organic synthesis) and is the only person who has reliably reverse-engineered Octavius's tentacle control schema.

**Combat.** Self-taught and structurally idiosyncratic. No formal martial training in the Lee/Ditko/Romita era; the fighting style is improvised acrobatic brawling layered over reflex faster than thought. Later runs (Bendis, Slott, Spencer) have him absorbing instruction from Shang-Chi, Iron Fist, and Captain America in pieces, but the core never becomes orthodox — his style remains *spider-shaped* (lateral, inverted, perpetually off-axis), because no orthodox style accommodates an opponent whose reflexes outpace their visual cortex.

**Photojournalism.** Genuine craft, financially exploitative arrangement. Decades of selling action shots to the Bugle of *himself*, often the only photographer who could obtain the angle. The instrument is typically a wide-angle film SLR mounted on a web-line or surface-anchored with a timer. The skill is real (composition, exposure, the ethical line between document and self-promotion he wrestled with publicly in the Wein and Mantlo runs).

**Teaching.** Demonstrated in the Slott high-school period and subsequent mentoring relationships (Anya Corazon, Miles Morales across the multiverse). The pedagogy is patient, anecdotal, self-deprecating. He teaches by making the student laugh at the problem.

**Improvisation under load.** The single most undervalued skill in his file. He has, on documented occasion, built functional engineering solutions from environmental materials mid-combat (the cure for the lizard serum, multiple iterations; the Octavius brain-pattern intercept). The improvisational capacity is the intellectualization defense (Section 3) operating at speed.

---

## 5. GROWTH OVER TIME

The trajectory is not strictly upward, and the file should be precise about this. Raw physical capacity has not appreciably changed since the bite — he is approximately as strong, fast, and adhesive at fifteen as at thirty-five. What has changed:

- **Spider-sense interpretation.** Early (Lee/Ditko) period: registers as undifferentiated tingling, sometimes panic-inducing. Mid (Romita through DeMatteis): graduated discrimination of threat type and magnitude. Mature (Slott onward): used as a multi-channel battlefield-awareness input integrated with visual and auditory streams without conscious attention. The power did not grow; the *interpretive cortex around it* matured.
- **Web-formulation.** Iterative refinement across continuous chemistry work over decades. The formulae of the 1990s and 2000s would not have been possible in 1965.
- **Combat economy.** Early Peter fights long and exhaustingly; mature Peter terminates engagements in single-digit seconds when conditions permit. The compression is a function of experience reading opponents, not enhanced capability.
- **Tactical use of identity.** Early Peter treats Spider-Man as suit-on / suit-off. Mature Peter treats the two as instruments to be deployed strategically — the civilian identity is increasingly used in operations (Slott, Spencer, Wells), though never comfortably.

What has *not* changed: the willingness to take the hit. Across sixty years of canon, Peter steps into harm's path with the same alacrity at thirty-five as at fifteen. This is not growth; this is the unchanged engine.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS

The combat signatures, ordered by frequency and diagnostic weight:

- **The mid-air web-line course-correction.** Releasing a swing line, falling, firing a second line at the last visible second to arrest the fall in an unexpected vector. Used routinely against opponents who track his trajectory. The willingness to fall *first* and shoot *second* is itself a signature of the personality (Section 5): he trusts the catch because the alternative is unbearable rest.
- **The talk-while-tagging.** Verbal output volume increases precisely in the windows during which he is placing a spider-tracer or scanning the opponent. Foes who have noticed (Octopus, Kingpin, Venom) have learned to attend to the tracer; foes who have not have lost.
- **Web-net deployment from elevation.** Civilian rescue signature. Net first, threat second.
- **The "lift the implausible object" beat.** Master Planner debris, fallen building components, escape-vehicle weight off a trapped civilian. The frequency of this image across his canon is the visual through-line of his moral structure (Section 5, drive #1).
- **The pulled punch.** A combat signature easy to overlook. He almost never strikes at full capacity against human opponents because full capacity is lethal. The micro-modulation of force per blow, in real time, against opponents whose durability he is estimating on the fly, is a continuous cognitive load most analysts underestimate.
- **The cover-the-civilian-with-the-body.** Default reflex against ordnance. He absorbs the blast or shrapnel with his own back. The reflex is sub-cortical; he does not decide it. (Clinical reading: the body is reliably more expendable to him than any other body in the frame.)
- **Dialogue under load.** Quipping volume rises monotonically with threat magnitude. See Section 7.

---

## 7. LIMITS — WHAT BREAKS HIM

**Sustained psionic attack.** The spider-sense routes through neurology that telepaths can interfere with; he is not psi-resistant. Has been mentally dominated repeatedly.

**Sonic weapons.** The acoustic sensitivity of the enhanced auditory channels is exploitable (the Shocker, Klaw, and the original anti-symbiote weapons all leverage this).

**Specific chemical agents.** Ethyl chloride and certain bio-pacifiers; ironically, certain pesticides marketed against ordinary arachnids have produced disproportionate reactions in canon (Mantlo, Conway).

**Immobilization.** The single most reliable break-state. Restrained, buried, or otherwise denied motion, his entire defense stack collapses (Section 3 — motion is one of three affect channels; close all three and the underlying state surfaces). Kraven's "Last Hunt" remains the demonstration case. Any villain who has been paying attention has noticed.

**Exhaustion.** The metabolic load means he can be ground down by attritional engagements faster than most peers. Sleep debt is cumulative across weeks and degrades both spider-sense fidelity and quip latency.

**Loss of the mask.** Tactical exposure of his identity converts his most reliable defense — the bifurcation between selves (Section 3) — into a vulnerability he cannot mitigate by power alone.

**The hostage problem.** Any opponent who has correctly identified May, MJ, or a child-equivalent figure has a guaranteed engagement-winning lever. He will sacrifice tactical position, alliance commitments, and personal autonomy in immediate sequence. Mephisto demonstrated the upper bound.

---

## 8. THE SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE READING

This is the section the file exists to make. Each of the subject's signature operational behaviors is, on examination, a psychiatric symptom that has been routed into a tactical channel by the engineering of the powers around it.

**The quip *is* the affect-regulation deficit.** It is not a separate stylistic flourish layered over the combat. It is the reaction-formation defense (Section 3) firing at the moments — and *only* at the moments — when the affect underneath is most likely to break through. It functions tactically (distracts opponents, reassures civilians, occupies his own panic so it cannot freeze him) because it functions psychiatrically (converts the unbearable into its opposite at the point of greatest pressure). Foes who attack his humor are attacking his regulation skill. He has no replacement. This is why being silenced under load — Kraven's burial — produces collapse rather than mere inconvenience.

**Spider-sense *is* the hypervigilance.** Or, more precisely: the post-traumatic hypervigilance has had a literal precognitive substrate to attach to, and the subject's nervous system has built its entire baseline arousal regulation around the assumption that the alarm is veridical. In a baseline human, hypervigilance is symptom; in this subject, it is also accurate. Both can be true. The cost is the same.

**The synthetic webbing *is* the intellectualization defense.** Externalized into the operational stack. His refusal to remain biologically web-spinning, post-"Other," is the defense reasserting itself against an imposed somatic gift. He needs the apparatus to be something he *built*, because being equipped by the world without his consent recapitulates the original violation — the bite he did not ask for.

**The body-over-civilian reflex *is* the guilt-organized altruism.** The Uncle Ben template (Section 1) running on hardware. His body is more expendable to him than any other body in any room he is in, and the spider-endowment has made this calculus survivable as a recurring practice rather than lethal on first execution.

**The pulled punch *is* the moral absolutism on no-kill.** The cognitive load of real-time force modulation is the price of the deontological commitment described in Section 4. He could end engagements faster by hitting harder; he does not. The decision is rebuilt each engagement, each blow.

**The mid-air course-correction *is* the relationship pattern.** He releases his anchor, falls, and fires a second line at the last moment. Read across to his attachment behavior (Section 5): pursuit, withdrawal, last-second recommitment. He trusts the catch because he has trained himself to trust the catch, and the catch is always his own engineering — which is to say, never quite anyone else.

**The Captain Universe and Iron Spider discards *are* the self-concept incoherence.** Power he did not earn through suffering is power he cannot integrate. The bargain is required to be costly or he does not believe it is real. (This is also why the Mephisto deal was structurally available to him as an option: a sacrifice that costs *everything* is, in his economy, the only sacrifice that registers.)

**The Superior interregnum's revealed ceiling *is* the diagnosis.** Octavius operated the same body at measurably higher tactical output. The differential is the patient. Peter has been running the apparatus at the throttle his guilt permits — generous enough to save, restrained enough to keep paying. This is the file's central finding on the powers question: the limits are not the spider's. They are his. And the limits *are* the structure of the man.

— END SECTION —


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

## SUBJECT: PARKER, PETER BENJAMIN ("SPIDER-MAN")

*Section 6 of UATU Dossier. Behavioral-operational mapping derived from canonical record (Lee/Ditko, Lee/Romita, Conway, DeFalco, DeMatteis, Michelinie, Bendis, JMS, Slott, Spencer, Wells runs; Civil War; Superior; Back in Black; Kraven's Last Hunt).*

---

## 6.1 DECISION ARCHITECTURE

The subject's operational decision-making is a hybrid system layered in three strata, and understanding the hierarchy is the predicate for predicting his behavior in any scenario.

**Stratum One — Spider-Sense Reflex (latency: 40–120 ms).** The proprioceptive precognitive alert overrides cortical deliberation entirely. Action at this layer is pre-conscious: dodge, web, reposition. He has described it (DeMatteis, Straczynski narration) as the body moving before the thought arrives. Operationally significant: the subject is essentially incapable of *not* dodging a sufficient threat, which means a hostile actor can manipulate his movement vector with predictable feints (Kraven exploited this; Doctor Octopus has repeatedly used it for misdirection). The reflex is suppressible only by exhaustion, sensory saturation, or chemical/psychic interference (the Mysterio gas, the Charlie/Ezekiel arc revelations).

**Stratum Two — Tactical Engineering (latency: seconds to minutes).** Mid-engagement and short-horizon planning operate through an engineering vocabulary. He reads environments structurally — load-bearing members, sightlines, fall vectors, conductive surfaces, fluid mechanics. Witness accounts and his own thought-bubble narration consistently show him computing in physics terms (mass, momentum, tensile strength, joules) rather than tactical-military terms (cover, flanking, breach). This is consequential: he wins engagements that resemble materials-science problems and loses engagements that resemble pure violence. He does not "fight," he *re-engineers the encounter*.

**Stratum Three — Moral Adjudication (latency: minutes to days, sometimes never).** The strategic layer is dominated by ethical re-litigation rather than outcome optimization. He will re-examine a successful operation if a civilian was endangered en route; he will accept a tactically suboptimal arrest method to preserve the no-kill rule; he will refuse intel from sources he considers compromised even when the intel is verified. This stratum runs slow, runs loud (he talks himself through it, often out loud while swinging), and is the layer most vulnerable to manipulation by anyone framing a moral appeal.

The critical operational fact about this architecture is that the three strata do not communicate well under stress. Stratum One can deliver him from a kill-zone while Stratum Three is still adjudicating whether the engagement was justified, producing the characteristic mid-fight self-interrogation that allies (Daredevil, the Human Torch) and enemies (the Kingpin, in particular) have catalogued as a signature tell.

---

## 6.2 OPERATIONAL TEMPO AND DAILY PATTERN

The subject runs on a bimodal twenty-four-hour cycle that has been remarkably stable across six decades of canon despite enormous variation in living arrangement, employment, and relationship status.

**Diurnal civilian envelope (variable, low-priority).** Day-job attendance is chronically poor. Across the Bugle freelance era (Lee through JMS), the Tri-Corp / Horizon Labs / Parker Industries / Threats & Menaces phases, the subject is reliably late by fifteen to ninety minutes, reliably under-delivers stated commitments, and reliably over-delivers technical output when actually present. The pattern is *not* laziness; it is the after-effect of the nocturnal envelope colonizing the diurnal one.

**Nocturnal operational envelope (priority, non-negotiable).** Primary patrol windows: roughly 21:00 to 02:00 weekdays, extended 19:00 to 04:00 weekends and crisis periods. Secondary "anomaly response" any hour, triggered by police scanner, news alert, or spider-sense. The subject has been depicted carrying a small portable scanner since the Lee/Romita era; in modern runs this has migrated to a phone application (Slott explicitly shows this; Spencer's run formalizes it with the "Threats & Menaces" feed).

**Transitional rituals.** The wardrobe change is itself tradecraft. Across canon he favors rooftops, alley dumpsters, abandoned construction sites, the Bugle photo-lab darkroom (Lee era), unused stairwells, his own apartment fire escape, and — when truly compromised — the inside of his own civilian coat with the costume worn beneath (the "shirt over the costume" depicted from Romita through to Bagley's Ultimate run is canonical). He has been observed by writers and artists to fold the costume into a remarkably small bundle, suggesting either deliberately thin fabric or a long-practiced packing routine. The mask is typically the last thing on and the first thing off; multiple panels show him with mask rolled to the bridge of the nose during transition, breathing through his mouth.

**Sleep architecture.** Chronic deficit. Two to four hours nightly under normal operations; zero during multi-day crises. He recovers in micro-naps — on rooftops, in subway cars, in the Bugle stockroom, slumped over a lab bench. The enhanced metabolism appears to permit functional performance at sleep loads that would incapacitate a baseline human, but the affective consequences (irritability, ruminative spiral, diminished impulse control on the quip) are visible.

---

## 6.3 MOVEMENT AND ROUTE TRADECRAFT

The subject's movement profile is the single most distinctive operational signature in the file.

**Primary modality — web-swinging.** Three-dimensional vector travel over Manhattan at roof-line altitude. Typical operational speed 30–60 mph in pendulum mode, peaking around 100 mph in burst. He prefers the avenues' north-south corridors during heavy crosstown traffic and reverses for the inverse case. He will not swing at altitudes below pedestrian sightline if avoidable (a deliberate civilian-protection heuristic — falling debris from a snapped web).

**Web-anchor patterns.** He anchors preferentially to corners (load distribution), to dark stone and steel (visibility/contrast), and avoids glass curtain walls except in emergencies (the webbing's adhesion characteristics on glass are inconsistent in canon, and he behaves as if he knows this). He does not anchor to occupied window-frames if avoidable. Anchor selection happens at Stratum One speed — he is rarely depicted "choosing" a swing point.

**Surface locomotion.** Ceilings, walls, undersides of bridges and overpasses, the rear faces of billboards. He routes preferentially along surfaces that allow him to invert or cling, which means his mental map of the city is not a flat street grid but a fully three-dimensional topology including HVAC routes, water tower clusters, and rooftop access points. He knows which buildings have rooftop doors that latch from outside, which have functional fire escapes, which have superintendents who chase trespassers — granular tenant-level knowledge accumulated over twenty-plus operational years.

**Counter-surveillance routing.** He varies patrol paths. Witnesses and writers have noted that he rarely takes the same route to or from any fixed location twice running. He uses building interiors as cut-throughs (vent shafts, stairwells, freight elevators) when he suspects observation. He has demonstrated awareness of helicopter surveillance angles (Civil War, Superior, Spencer's "Threats & Menaces" arc) and will deliberately swing under overhangs to break aerial sightlines.

**Fixed-residence concealment.** His various apartments (the Chelsea walk-up, the Tribeca loft during the Stark-funded period, Aunt May's Forest Hills house, the FEAST shelter shared room with MJ, the Brooklyn share with Boomerang, the various Horizon and Parker Industries-adjacent units) are reliably entered through windows rather than doors during operational hours. Building neighbors across multiple addresses have reported (in-canon) sightings of "that weirdo who climbs in his own window." The subject has occasionally moved residence specifically to escape such accumulating observation.

---

## 6.4 EQUIPMENT, MATERIEL, AND THE WEB-FLUID PROBLEM

The subject is, materially speaking, almost entirely a single-piece-of-equipment operator: the web-shooters and the chemistry that feeds them.

**Web-shooter design.** Self-designed and self-fabricated as a teenager (AF #15; design refined continuously through Lee/Ditko/Romita and revisited in every subsequent run). Wrist-mounted; trigger is a double-tap palm pressure to prevent accidental discharge during normal hand use. Multiple nozzle settings (single line, spray, net, glob) selectable by trigger duration and angle. The design philosophy is significant: he could long ago have integrated organic web-glands (briefly canonical, the Disney-era organic webbing), and yet his preference is consistently *external, removable, repairable* equipment. This is consistent with the broader psychological pattern — keep the spider on the outside, where it can be taken off.

**Web-fluid chemistry.** A shear-thinning polymer of his own formulation, dissolves on a roughly one-hour timer. Recipe is closely held. He carries spare cartridges in a belt under the costume (typically six, sometimes eight; he runs out during long engagements and this is a frequent narrative crisis — Lee, DeMatteis, JMS, Slott all use it). Cartridge fabrication is a recurring time-and-money sink that intersects directly with his financial precarity: when broke, he is operationally degraded.

**Costume.** Material varies by era but the operational features are stable: full-face mask with one-way lenses (eye-lenses occasionally explicitly described as polarized or as containing optical correctives — Slott's Horizon-era upgrades); thin breathable fabric tolerant of stretch and impact; integrated belt for cartridges and miniature camera (Lee through Bendis era — the spider-tracer-camera setup he sells to Jameson). He owns multiple identical suits, hand-washed in his own sink, hung over the shower rod to dry; the iconic visual of a costume drying in a bathroom is a recurrent canonical image (Romita, Bagley, McNiven).

**Spider-tracers.** Miniature radio transmitters keyed to his spider-sense; he scatters these on suspects, vehicles, and crime scenes for later tracking. The technology is functionally a personal-area surveillance grid. Range, battery life, and detection methodology have varied by writer, but the *practice* of pre-tagging adversaries is a stable element of his tradecraft from Lee onward.

**What he does NOT carry.** No firearm, ever. No edged weapon. No lethal countermeasures of any kind. No body armor beyond the suit. No comms link to law enforcement (he refuses formal channel). No backup-summoning beacon for most of canon — when allied (FF, Avengers, post-Civil War), he carries Avengers comms but is famously inconsistent about answering them.

**The camera.** Critical operational asset throughout the Bugle-photographer phase. A small automatic-trigger 35mm body, modified to fire on web-cued remote, clipped to a fixed surface during engagements. The camera is the income engine; without it, the subject cannot eat. This is a recursive operational vulnerability — to make money, he must photograph himself committing the very heroics that endanger him, which means his survival economy is wedded to his trauma cycle.

---

## 6.5 FINANCIAL PATTERN

Financial behavior is a signature in itself.

**Income.** Chronically inadequate and chronically irregular. Bugle freelance photography (decades, variable rate, frequently disputed by Jameson); brief stints as substitute teacher (Forest Hills High, Conway-era); science consultant (Tri-Corp, JMS); Horizon Labs researcher (Slott — by far his most stable and best-paid period, abruptly ended); CEO of Parker Industries (Slott — anomalously wealthy briefly, lost entirely); Daily Bugle / Threats & Menaces digital again (Spencer/Wells). The career arc is sawtooth: ascent, catastrophic loss, return to baseline.

**Outflows.** Rent (chronically late); web-fluid chemistry costs (estimated by Slott-era narration in the low thousands monthly at full operational tempo); equipment repair; medical (he avoids ER's for cost and identification reasons, but has accepted underground-doctor care — the "Night Nurse" / Linda Carter circuit); food (high caloric requirement); contributions to Aunt May.

**Cash discipline.** Poor in normal range, excellent under extreme constraint. He will skip meals before he asks for help. He has been depicted (Conway, DeMatteis, Slott) calculating subway fare versus a long swing home; he has counted change at bodegas. The shame of poverty operates as a separate motivational force.

**The non-monetization principle.** He has been offered, refused, or sabotaged paid superheroism repeatedly. He will not patent the webbing (despite explicit canonical opportunities). He will not license the likeness. He has refused Stark money and Avengers stipend at multiple junctures. The principle reads as ethical (heroism must not be transactional), but functions psychologically as preservation of the guilt-debt structure — accepting payment would close the Uncle Ben ledger, and the ledger must remain open.

---

## 6.6 INTELLIGENCE COLLECTION AND SOURCING

He is, despite no formal training, an unusually competent HUMINT collector at the street level.

**Informant network.** Across decades he has cultivated low-level informants in Hell's Kitchen, the Lower East Side, Harlem, and outer-borough criminal substrata. Methodology is non-coercive: he dangles informants upside down for theatrical effect, then talks. The interrogation style is verbose, disarming, occasionally absurd — and surprisingly productive. Suspects relax under the joking and reveal more than they intend. This is a deliberate technique, refined over years; it is not accidental affect bleed.

**Open-source intelligence.** Heavy police-scanner usage; in modern eras, social media monitoring, news app subscriptions, the Threats & Menaces feed itself functioning as a self-reinforcing OSINT loop. He reads Bugle crime reports for tip leads — recursively, since he often photographed the original incidents.

**Liaison.** Selective and trust-based rather than institutional. Captain Stacy (until death), Captain Jean DeWolff (until death — note the pattern), Yuri Watanabe (until her moral collapse — note the pattern again), assorted patrol officers. He does not coordinate with FBI, SHIELD on principle, or the DA's office. The pattern of liaison-figure death/corruption has measurably increased his reluctance to develop new institutional contacts; he treats every new uniformed contact as a future loss.

**Allied superhuman liaison.** Daredevil (most trusted), the Human Torch (closest non-romantic friendship across canon), Black Cat (compromised by intimacy), the Fantastic Four collectively, the Avengers situationally, Doctor Strange for esoteric problems. He shares information selectively even with close allies — the secret-keeping behavior bleeds into operational compartmentalization.

---

## 6.7 ENGAGEMENT DOCTRINE

Stable across canon with rare deviation:

1. **De-escalate by talk first.** The quipping is not only psychological self-regulation; it is also functional verbal de-escalation when facing low-tier opposition, and functional psychological warfare against ego-organized opposition (it provokes Doc Ock, Vulture, Shocker into mistakes).
2. **Civilian extraction before pursuit.** He will lose an adversary rather than risk a bystander. This is exploitable and has been exploited.
3. **Property over persons.** He will destroy his own webbing-budget, the immediate environment, vehicles, and infrastructure freely to avoid bodily harm to anyone, including the opponent.
4. **Capture, do not kill.** Absolute. The no-kill rule has held against Carnage, the Green Goblin post-Gwen, Kraven, and the Sin-Eater — opponents against whom utilitarian argument for lethal force is at its strongest.
5. **Webbed to a lamppost for the morning shift.** Standard disposition for street-level adversaries: web-bind, attach to fixed civic infrastructure, leave for police, photograph for Bugle. The ritual has been visually identical from Ditko through Wells.
6. **Withdraw when outmatched.** He will swing away. This is operationally important — he does not have a tactical ego about retreat — but he returns, usually faster than is wise, after recalibration.

**Engagement *failures*** cluster in identifiable scenarios: opponents who exploit the no-kill rule (Kraven's son, Carnage); opponents who target attachment figures to bypass his tactical doctrine entirely (Goblin, every iteration); opponents who immobilize him (Kraven's burial, Octavius's body-theft); opponents who deny him the quip channel by sustained psychological pressure (Venom's symbiote knowledge; Mysterio's reality manipulation).

---

## 6.8 INFRASTRUCTURE

The subject maintains a notably *thin* operational infrastructure for an actor of his longevity and threat profile.

**Safehouses.** None formally. He treats Aunt May's Forest Hills house as fallback (compromised, repeatedly); the Baxter Building and Avengers Tower as occasional crash spaces (politically variable); Doctor Strange's Sanctum for esoteric crisis. The Parker Industries period briefly gave him global infrastructure which he visibly mismanaged and is, in retrospect, characteristic — he is not constitutionally suited to operating *as* an institution.

**Workshops.** The basement at May's house (decades); the Bugle darkroom (early career); the Tri-Corp lab; the Horizon Labs personal lab (his happiest professional period by some distance — depicted by Slott as the only place he sleeps soundly); various apartment kitchens converted to chemistry stations with characteristically inadequate ventilation. He has burned at least three rental units' worth of countertop with web-fluid spills.

**Communications.** Phone (always cheap, frequently broken, frequently lost); Avengers comm (situational); landline at May's (sentimental retention long after obsolete). He resists biometric devices, smart assistants, anything that produces a persistent data exhaust. The instinct precedes the threat model — he was protective of personal data before he had reason to be.

**Document tradecraft.** Negligible. He has never operated under a sustained alternate identity. The "Spider-Man" persona functions as the alternate, and the bifurcation is total, not layered. He carries his actual driver's license while in costume (canonical embarrassment in multiple runs — captured, unmasked, identified instantly).

---

## 6.9 SIGNATURE TELLS — OPERATIONAL AND BEHAVIORAL

These are the granular tells a surveillance file accumulates over years and which, in aggregate, identify the subject more reliably than any single biometric.

- **The verbal envelope expands inversely with safety margin.** Quip volume and density rise as actual danger rises. Total silence from the subject mid-combat is the strongest single indicator that he is genuinely terrified or genuinely grieving.
- **Mid-swing self-interrogation.** He talks to himself out loud during transit. Witnesses have reported overhearing entire ethical debates conducted between two skyscrapers.
- **Head tilt on spider-sense.** Sub-conscious lateral head movement at the onset of the alert, three to five degrees, repeatable. Combat opponents have learned to read this.
- **Knuckle-rub on the mask.** Stress tell — he rubs the bridge of the nose through the fabric. Visible to artists from Romita onward.
- **The crouch.** Resting posture is a deep squat with weight on the balls of the feet, hands loose between knees, more often than seated. He sits *on* furniture less than he perches on it. In civilian dress he catches himself doing this in inappropriate contexts and corrects.
- **Window entry.** He will enter a room he is invited to through the window if the window is available. This is decades-stable.
- **Late arrival, breathless, with implausible explanation.** The civilian signature. The implausibility is so consistent it has itself become recognizable; MJ, May, and Robbie Robertson have all named it.
- **Hand-washing of equipment.** Costume, web-shooters, cartridges — manual maintenance done at the kitchen sink. He does not delegate equipment care even when teammates offer.
- **Photographing himself.** The Bugle-camera economics produced a decades-long habit of staging self-documentation during operations. He still reaches for a camera mount reflexively in modern eras even when no longer freelancing.
- **The pause before naming the dead.** When operational debrief requires reference to Ben, Gwen, Jean DeWolff, Captain Stacy, Marla Jameson — a measurable hesitation precedes the name. The pause has not shortened with time.
- **Refusal of thanks.** Civilians attempting to thank him post-rescue receive a joke, a wave, and a fast exit. He will accelerate his withdrawal specifically to escape gratitude. This is the most consistent civilian-facing tell in the entire file.
- **Eating standing up, fast, large quantities, often cold.** The metabolic demand combined with operational tempo has produced a long-stable food behavior visible to roommates and partners across runs.
- **Apologizing pre-emptively.** Conversational tic. He apologizes for things that have not yet happened and may not. Partners across canon have noted it; MJ has named it directly.

---

## 6.10 OPERATIONAL VULNERABILITIES (FORWARD-PLANNING)

Compiled for analyst use, not for exploitation:

1. Any credible threat to a named attachment figure collapses tactical doctrine to a single vector and makes the subject's movements perfectly predictable.
2. Immobilization scenarios (restraint, burial, confinement, body-occupation) produce disproportionate psychological harm relative to physical risk.
3. Financial pressure operationally degrades him via the web-fluid supply chain; sustained economic disruption is a more effective degradation than physical engagement.
4. Sleep denial compounds. He is functional at three hours; he is dangerous to himself and others at zero across multiple days.
5. The moral-adjudication stratum is exploitable by any opponent willing to construct a plausible ethical dilemma faster than he can resolve it. Hostages remain the master case.
6. Public unmasking is a stratum-three catastrophe whose downstream effects exceed the tactical consequences by orders of magnitude (Civil War as the type-case).
7. The refusal to develop institutional support means he absorbs systemic problems individually and deg


## Worldview & Operational Code

# Worldview & Operational Code — SUBJECT: PARKER, P. B.

*Derived from sixty years of behavioral record. This section maps the subject's complete cognitive-ethical operating system: the working metaphysics, the rules of engagement, the trust architecture, the risk calculus, and the implicit theology of his own place in the order. None of this is articulated by the subject as a system; he would deny he has one. The system is nevertheless visible, internally consistent, and astonishingly stable across decades.*

---

## 1. The Implicit Metaphysics

The subject operates under a working cosmology that is neither religious nor secular in any clean sense. It is best described as **a moral universe without a moral guarantor**. The world, in his lived experience, contains real good and real evil, real cause and real consequence — and *no one whose job it is to ensure the books balance*. The books balance only if someone in the room makes them balance. That someone, by default and by debt, is him.

The substrate beliefs, reconstructed from behavior:

- **The universe is causally responsive but not just.** Effort produces results; results are not proportional to virtue. Good people die at random. The thief who killed Ben was not a cosmic agent of punishment; he was a man Peter could have stopped and didn't. The cosmos did not arrange the lesson. Peter arranged it, by omission, and the cosmos merely permitted it. This is critical: he does not believe in fate, karma, or divine ordering. He believes in *negligence* — his own and others' — as the primary engine of suffering.

- **Power is not a gift, an entitlement, or a neutral fact. Power is a debt instrument.** The famous formulation ("with great power…") is not, in his private operation, an aphorism. It is a *ledger entry*. He received capability; he therefore owes a corresponding quantum of service. The debt cannot be paid down in any final sense — every life saved generates the next obligation to save the next — but it can be defaulted on, and default is the only mortal sin in his system.

- **Death is the irreversible category.** Almost nothing else in his universe is permanent — bodies regenerate, identities recover, even some of the dead return (Harry, Norman, Kraven, even Peter himself) — but his operational code treats every death as if it will be the final one. He does not factor resurrection into planning. This is not naivete; it is moral hygiene. To plan around the possibility of undoing death is to soften the constraint that organizes his entire ethics.

- **Time is not a healer; time is a witness.** Old wounds remain present-tense for him. Gwen falling is not a memory; it is an event that is still occurring somewhere in the structure of his consciousness. This means his moral universe is *additive* — failures accumulate, they do not decay — which produces the load-bearing exhaustion visible across every long arc.

- **There is no neutral bystander position.** To witness and not act is to act. The thief sequence taught this once and for all. Any time he is in proximity to harm and does not intervene, he has *chosen* the harm. The consequence: he cannot ever be off-duty in any conscience-satisfying way. He can be tired, he can be late, he can fail — but he cannot legitimately be uninvolved.

---

## 2. The Reading of Conflict

Conflict, to the subject, is **almost never about the conflict itself**. He is one of the few combatants of his class who genuinely does not enjoy fighting and does not narrate fighting to himself in heroic terms. Combat, in his internal frame, is *failure already in progress* — the situation has already deteriorated to the point where talk has stopped working, and his job is to compress the damage.

His combat read is consequently shaped by four operating principles:

- **Minimize the duration.** Every additional second of combat is additional opportunity for a civilian to be hurt, for a building to collapse, for him to make a mistake. This is why he opens fights with maximal verbal and physical disruption: the patter is partly defense, but it is also a *tempo weapon* — he is trying to derail the opponent's plan before it executes. He fights to end fights, not to win them.

- **The opponent is a person until proven otherwise.** Even with Octavius, Osborn, Kraven, Connors, Morbius — particularly with Connors and Morbius, men whose monstrosity is involuntary — he reads the fight as something happening *to* the opponent as much as against them. This is why he hesitates to use lethal force in situations where lethal force is tactically indicated, and why he repeatedly accepts injury he could have avoided by escalating. The hesitation is not weakness of will; it is a deliberate moral stance that the cost of being wrong about the opponent's humanity is unacceptable.

- **Property is expendable; bodies, his own included to a point, are not.** He will let a building come down to catch a falling child. He will let himself be hit to keep an opponent's strike off a bystander. He will not, however, let civilians be used as pawns to make him surrender — he has learned (the hard way, repeatedly) that surrender does not save the hostage, it merely adds him to the hostage count.

- **Conflict is data.** He is a scientist mid-fight. He profiles opponents in real time — gait, breathing, tells, weight distribution, the specific torque of a punch — and he updates fast. The quipping covers the analysis; while he is talking, he is also building a working model of the opponent's nervous system. Watch closely across the canon: the second exchange with any given foe is markedly more efficient than the first.

He does not believe in the redemptive function of violence. He does not believe villains learn from being beaten. He believes the beating is a *containment* — a way of buying time for the systems that might, possibly, fix the underlying problem (the law, medicine, the rare actual rehabilitation). When the systems fail, as they often do, he absorbs the failure as additional debt rather than concluding that more violence is the answer.

---

## 3. The Reading of Control

The subject's relationship to control is **deeply ambivalent and asymmetric**. He requires extensive control over his own behavior, his secret, his exposure, his tactical environment — and is constitutionally hostile to control exercised *over* him by institutions or individuals.

The components:

- **Self-control is moral.** Restraint — of force, of anger, of grief, of need — is the index of whether he is still the man Ben raised. Every time he does not kill the Goblin after Gwen, every time he does not break Jameson's jaw, every time he does not lean on MJ when he most wants to — these are his proofs to himself. The discipline is the demonstration. Loss of self-control is, for him, indistinguishable from moral collapse, which is why the rare episodes of explosive rage are so psychologically expensive afterward.

- **Institutional control is suspect by default.** This is consistent from his earliest Jameson conflicts through Civil War. He extends provisional trust to institutions when they produce visible good (the police, on a case-by-case basis; the Avengers, conditionally) and withdraws it instantly when they produce visible harm. The registration arc is the clarifying datum: he initially complied — out of his characteristic deference to a father-figure (Stark) presenting a credible argument — and reversed completely the moment he saw the prison and understood the mechanism. His test for institutional legitimacy is empirical and ongoing, not ideological.

- **He will not control others.** This is unusual and worth flagging. With his capabilities he could dominate civilians, intimidate opponents into permanent compliance, or organize networks of subordinate operatives; he does none of these. The Superior arc — in which Octavius, in his body, immediately begins acquiring property, building organizations, intimidating rivals, taking on subordinates — is the explicit counter-image of what Peter could be and refuses to be. He has a near-absolute discomfort with being *in charge*, declining team leadership repeatedly, taking it only when the alternative is worse.

- **Control over the secret is non-negotiable, until it is.** The dual-identity wall is the structural feature that keeps the system standing (see §5). He defends it ferociously, and the few times it has come down (Civil War, various alternate reveals) he has paid grievously. But — and this is the part the file should not miss — he reveals selectively and deliberately to those he loves, often early in the relationship, *as a test*. He cannot tolerate love-without-disclosure; the secret must be shared with the chosen few precisely so that he can know the love is for the whole organism, not the cover story.

---

## 4. The Architecture of Trust

Trust, in the subject's system, is built on **demonstrated behavior under cost**, not on credentials, reputation, alliance, or even kinship. He has been betrayed often enough — by mentors (Octavius, originally a respected scientist), by friends (Harry, repeatedly), by institutions (the Bugle, the registration apparatus), by his own body (Superior) — that he has developed a layered trust system:

- **Inner ring (unconditional, irrevocable):** May. MJ (across all canonical configurations, regardless of in-universe relationship status). The dead — Ben, Gwen, Captain Stacy, Jean DeWolff — who function as a permanent conscience-jury. Trust here is structural; it does not need to be re-earned and cannot be lost.

- **Second ring (deep, durable, slowly built):** A small set including the Human Torch, Daredevil, the Black Cat (complicated), select X-figures (Logan, despite obvious dissimilarity), and at times Stark and Richards. These are people who have proven they will absorb cost on his behalf without ledger-keeping. Trust at this layer is robust to a great deal of friction; one bad day does not collapse it.

- **Third ring (working trust, conditional, revocable):** Most colleagues, allies of convenience, professional contacts. Extended freely on a presumption of good faith, withdrawn on first evidence of bad faith. He is unusually quick to *re*-extend trust after rupture if the rupture is repaired — a function of his deep belief in the redeemability of persons.

- **The bystander default:** Civilians are trusted to be worth saving, full stop. He does not screen victims for worthiness. The man in the burning building is the man in the burning building. This is one of the operational facts that distinguishes him most sharply from peers who have drifted into utilitarian triage.

- **The opponent class:** Trusted to act on their stated motives until they demonstrate otherwise, which is often. He is repeatedly fooled by villains feigning reform, and this should not be read as stupidity. He is making a deliberate moral wager — that the cost of being wrong about a sincere reformation is far worse than the cost of being wrong about a feigned one. He would rather be exploited than calcified.

Distrust, when it forms, is exceptionally durable. He has never fully trusted Norman Osborn again; he has never fully trusted Stark since the registration arc; he has never fully trusted his own body since Superior. The trust system is forgiving in the small and unforgiving at the cardinal level.

---

## 5. The Risk Calculus

The subject's risk calculus is **systematically asymmetric** in ways that would be irrational in any other operator but are internally coherent given his foundational ethics.

The calculus, decomposed:

- **Risk to self is steeply discounted.** Not zero — he wants to live, he is afraid of dying, he experiences pain normally — but discounted relative to any comparable risk to a third party. A 10% chance of a civilian death will be traded against a 90% chance of his own. This is not bravery in the conventional sense; it is the Uncle Ben template enforcing itself at the level of marginal decision-making.

- **Risk to attachment figures is treated as infinite.** Any non-zero probability of harm to May, MJ, or a surrogate triggers an override that bypasses tactical reasoning entirely. This is the known exploit and every sophisticated villain has used it. He knows it is an exploit and cannot disarm it.

- **Risk to the secret is treated as quasi-infinite,** for reasons discussed above and in §3 — exposure of the identity proliferates risk to the inner ring without ceiling.

- **Risk to mission integrity** (the ongoing work of being Spider-Man) is weighed against immediate human cost, and immediate cost always wins. He will burn long-term operational capital — a hard-won identity with a villain, an investigation in progress, a tactical advantage — to prevent a near-term death. This is part of why he never accumulates the kind of strategic depth that comparable operators (Murdock as Daredevil, Wayne in his universe) do; he spends his capital constantly.

- **Risk to personal stability** (job, rent, relationships, sleep, his degree) is treated as essentially free. This is the "Parker Luck" pattern from the inside: he does not, strictly, get unlucky. He systematically prices his own stability at near zero and is then surprised when it is gone. The pricing is consistent with a self-concept in which his civilian life is the *less real* of the two lives (see §6) and therefore the legitimate sink for cost.

- **Risk of moral compromise is treated as catastrophic.** A 1% chance that an action will move him a millimeter toward becoming the kind of man who kills, who breaks faith, who lets a child fall — this risk dominates all others. It is the only risk class he refuses to negotiate. He will accept overwhelming probability of his own death to avoid small probability of moral drift.

The internal coherence: every weight in the calculus is set by reference to the foundational debt. The body is collateral. Stability is collateral. Operational capital is collateral. The only assets the system protects without compromise are *other people's lives* and *his own moral coherence*, because those are the two things the debt was incurred against.

---

## 6. Self and Place — The Implicit Theology of His Own Position

This is the section the subject would resist most strongly. He would say he doesn't think about himself this way. He doesn't have to; the operating code reveals what the conscious account omits.

- **He occupies the world as a man under sentence, working off a term.** Not in misery — he is capable of joy, particularly mid-swing, mid-quip, with MJ, with May, in the lab — but the joy is parenthetical to the work. The sentence has no defined end. The work is the life.

- **The two selves are not equally real to him.** The Spider-Man self is competent, witnessed, useful, *finished* — a functioning instrument. The Peter self is unfinished, failing, indebted, the *origin* of the obligation that the Spider-Man self discharges. He experiences the mask as the more honest of the two faces, which is the inverse of the standard secret-identity psychology. The mask is where he is allowed to be the man he is trying to become; the bare face is where he confronts the man he is afraid he still is.

- **He believes — operationally, not articulately — that he is the worst-positioned man to do his job and also the only man who can do it.** This is not arrogance; it is the inverse. The job is his because the debt is his. No one else is obligated. Others may help, and he is grateful when they do, but the obligation does not transfer.

- **He does not believe he deserves to be loved, and is loved anyway, and treats this as a standing miracle he must not break.** The pattern with MJ across every continuity confirms this. He is, beneath the patter, perpetually astonished that she chose him and chooses him; he protects the choice with everything he has; he cannot accept the love as straightforwardly his, which is why he gives it back in service rather than receiving it as rest.

- **He believes the small acts matter most.** This is one of the most under-noticed elements of his operational code. He goes back for the wallet. He fixes the kid's bike. He stops to give directions in costume. He helps the elderly woman across the street. These are not PR; he does them when no one is looking. His ethics are not scaled to cosmic stakes — he saves the universe when required, but he does not feel more virtuous saving the universe than helping a stranger. The small acts may, in fact, be where the system most truly lives, because they are the acts that confirm the work is *about other people*, not about his significance.

- **He believes he is replaceable in the role and irreplaceable in the obligation.** Others can be Spider-Man (Miles, Ben Reilly, even Octavius in his fashion); only he can pay *his* debt. This distinction — between the function, which is transferable, and the obligation, which is not — is the cleanest single statement of his place-in-the-world model.

---

## 7. Operational Code: The Rules, Reconstructed

If the subject were to write down the rules he actually operates by — which he never would — they would read approximately as follows. These are induced from behavior, not from any stated creed.

1. **If you can act, you must.** Inaction in the presence of preventable harm is the cardinal sin.
2. **Save first; understand later.** Diagnosis can wait until the bleeding stops.
3. **Do not kill.** Not because killing is metaphysically forbidden but because *you* must not become the kind of man who has.
4. **Talk through it.** The patter is the proof of life — both yours and the situation's. If you stop talking, you have stopped being yourself.
5. **The mask comes off only by your choice, and only for someone you have already decided to risk everything for.**
6. **Your civilian life is the sink, not the source. Spend it. Don't expect to keep it.**
7. **Owe nothing to power. Owe everything to people.**
8. **Authority is provisional. Re-test it constantly. Defy it the instant it fails.**
9. **The small kindness is not less than the great rescue. Do both.**
