10. **Be late, be tired, be hurt, be broke, be alone — but be there when it matters.**
11. **Do not accept the praise. The praise is for the function; the debt is still yours.**
12. **Protect the inner ring with everything. Protect strangers with almost everything. Protect yourself with what is left.**
13. **When you fail — and you will — log it, carry it, do not put it down. The carrying is part of the price.**
14. **If you have to choose between being a hero and being a good man, choose the good man. The hero only matters because the man does.**
15. **End the fight as fast as possible. The fight is not the point. The world after the fight is the point.**

---

## 8. Stability of the Code Over Time

The most analytically striking feature of the subject's worldview is its **resistance to revision**. He has been offered, repeatedly and at great pressure, alternative operating codes:

- The utilitarian-strategic frame (Stark, Fury): rejected, accepted briefly under filial pressure, rejected definitively.
- The vigilante-lethal frame (Punisher, various dark mirrors): rejected without serious consideration.
- The withdrawal frame (give it up, live a normal life, MJ has at points genuinely asked): seriously considered, repeatedly attempted, never sustained.
- The cosmic-empowerment frame (the various totem and Captain Universe arcs, the Other): experienced, integrated somatically, *not* allowed to alter the ethics.
- The body-thief / replacement frame (Superior): forced upon him, survived, reinforced the original code rather than weakening it.

Across sixty years of canon, in which comparable subjects (Stark, Richards, Banner, even Rogers at moments) show measurable ethical drift, the subject's operational code has remained **structurally identical to the one consolidated in his eighteenth year**. The pathological etiology of this stability is described in §3 of the analytical basis. The operational consequence is what concerns this file: the subject is among the most *predictable* high-capability operators in the dossier system, and his predictability is not weakness. It is the load-bearing fact about him. Adversaries who have understood this — Kraven most clearly, Octavius eventually — have been able to construct elaborate traps around it. Allies who have understood it have been able to rely on him absolutely.

The code is the man. The man is the debt. The debt is the work. And the work, for as long as the subject is functional, will not stop.

— END SECTION —


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

*Subject: PARKER, PETER BENJAMIN. File section 7 of working dossier. All claims derived from the longitudinal behavioral record; clinical framing per Chapman 2019 (PMID 31169118) and the workup above.*

---

## 7.1 The Code, As Enacted (Not As Professed)

The professed code is the famous formulation — *with great power comes great responsibility* — and the subject will recite it, or a variant, when pressed by interlocutors who want a thesis statement. This is not, however, the operative code. The operative code, derived from sixty years of decisions made under duress, is a deeper and more idiosyncratic structure with the following enacted axioms, listed in the order of behavioral priority observable in the record:

1. **No one dies if I can prevent it.** Not the bystander. Not the bank robber. Not the supervillain who, given thirty more seconds of liberty, will kill someone else. The operative unit is *the individual life in front of me right now*, and his prioritization of immediate-rescuable life over abstract aggregated harm is consistent across runs.
2. **I do not kill.** Even where utilitarian calculus would license it. Even where the same villain has, demonstrably, returned to kill again. Even when killing would prevent the death of someone he loves. (Carnage, Kraven, Norman Osborn pre-and-post-Gwen, the Sin-Eater debate after DeWolff, Morlun — the rule holds. Where it appears to break, examine subsection 7.4.)
3. **I do not let civilians take the cost meant for me.** He will interpose his body — every writer depicts this reflex — between any attack and any uninvolved person, including persons who an hour earlier were spitting at him from the sidewalk.
4. **I do not lie about what I have done wrong.** He will lie *prolifically* about what he is (the mask), about where he was, about why he is late — but when confronted with a moral failure of his own, he confesses, often unprompted, often to the wrong audience (he has confessed to enemies in the middle of fights). Self-incrimination is constitutive.
5. **I do not trade another person's autonomy for my comfort.** He will trade his *own* autonomy freely — body, marriage, identity, future — but he is markedly resistant to imposing on others. (The single famous exception is "One More Day," addressed below as a fracture.)
6. **I do not refuse a call.** If he hears someone scream, he goes. The cost — to job, relationship, sleep, health — is not weighed in the moment; the going is automatic. This is the axiom that produces the so-called "Parker Luck": the code itself is the saboteur.

These six axioms, in this order, predict his behavior in the field with approximately ninety percent reliability across the canon. The professed *power/responsibility* formula is a *justification* generated atop them, not a derivation that produces them.

---

## 7.2 Provenance of the Code

The code is not philosophical in origin. It is forensic. Each axiom traces to a specific wound:

- **Axiom 1** (*no one dies if I can prevent it*) is the inverse of the Uncle Ben omission. The thief he let pass became the killer; therefore every passed-by stranger is a potential killer of someone's uncle. The code is built backward from the failure.
- **Axiom 2** (*no killing*) is the most psychologically motivated of the rules and the least philosophically defended. He has, when challenged, given multiple incompatible justifications: that killing makes him "like them," that it would devastate May, that one death licenses the next, that the law must hold. None of these is the real reason. The real reason, derivable from his internal monologue in DeMatteis's Kraven and Slott's post-Superior arcs, is that he privately believes he is already a killer (Ben), and any further killing would confirm a self-concept he is barely holding closed. The no-kill rule is a containment wall around his self-image.
- **Axiom 3** (*interposition*) is Ben's death restaged with the inputs reversed — this time he is between the bullet and the person.
- **Axiom 4** (*confession*) is the residue of the foundational secret he could not tell May and could not tell Ben in time. Honesty about wrongdoing is the corrective he could not apply when it mattered.
- **Axiom 5** (*autonomy*) is the negative imprint of his own repeated experience of having his autonomy violated — the bite itself, the body-theft, the manipulations by Mysterio, the Jackal, Norman Osborn. Having been *used*, he is fastidious about not using.
- **Axiom 6** (*answer the call*) is the simplest: any unanswered call is a potential Ben.

This forensic provenance explains why the code is held with religious intensity but defended with rhetorical incoherence. It is not an argument; it is a scar.

---

## 7.3 The Granular Field-Level Code

In operation, the axioms generate a thicket of micro-rules visible in his moment-to-moment conduct:

- **He webs hands before mouths.** Across thousands of capture sequences, the pattern holds — disable the weapon, not the speech. Even hostile suspects retain voice. He will tolerate being insulted at length by a man he has just bound.
- **He pulls strikes against unenhanced humans.** Slott and Bendis both depict his internal calibration: a full-strength hit kills, therefore each blow is consciously throttled. He is one of very few combatants in his peer group who must perform this calculation in every engagement; the cognitive overhead is constant and uncredited.
- **He webs falls he caused.** If a thrown opponent is going through a window, he webs the opponent mid-air to the building, or webs the bystanders inside the window first. The corrective is reflexive.
- **He does not finish downed opponents.** Even when the opponent will rise in ninety seconds and resume trying to kill him. He gives the ninety seconds.
- **He refuses payment for rescue.** He will accept payment for *photographs* of Spider-Man (a separate moral category in his mind — labor, not heroism), but he has never accepted a reward for saving a life, and on several occasions has fled the scene to avoid being offered one.
- **He warns before he engages, where possible.** The pre-fight quip serves this function operationally as well as psychologically — it announces presence, gives the opponent the chance to disengage, and converts an ambush into a duel.
- **He apologizes mid-fight.** To civilians caught in property damage. To opponents he has hit harder than intended. To MJ, in his head, when he is late. The apology reflex is constant.
- **He does not unmask defeated foes uninvited.** Even when knowing the identity would yield tactical advantage. The mask is sacred property because his own is.
- **He brings injured enemies to hospitals, not precincts.** Documented repeatedly — the medical claim outweighs the legal one when both are pending.

These micro-rules are not articulated by the subject. They are observable only longitudinally. Their consistency across writers is the strongest evidence that the code is structurally his, not authorially imposed.

---

## 7.4 Where The Code Is Consistent

The consistencies are striking and worth itemizing because they constitute the strongest datum in the entire file. Across six decades, multiple writers, multiple universes, and conditions designed by adversaries to break exactly this structure, the following have held without significant exception:

- **The no-kill rule against human-class opponents.** It has been tested by Kraven (who killed himself rather than be killed), by Carnage (mass murderer, repeatedly spared), by Norman Osborn (the murderer of Gwen, spared again and again), by the Sin-Eater (the murderer of Jean DeWolff, where Daredevil's restraint was the mirror argument), by the Goblin in countless successors. He has come within a frame of breaking it — the post-Gwen beating of Osborn, the post-DeWolff confrontation — and stopped. The wall holds.
- **The body-as-shield reflex.** From AF #15 onward. He has never, under any documented stressor, allowed a civilian to take a hit he could intercept. This is the single most reliable behavioral prediction in the file.
- **The refusal to use lethal force on non-villains who are obstructing him.** Cops trying to arrest him, soldiers under orders, mind-controlled allies — he disengages, he evades, he webs and runs. He does not hurt people who are wrong but not evil.
- **The refusal of money for heroism.**
- **The refusal to abandon the mission once accepted.** He has, across runs, finished patrols with cracked ribs, concussions, a broken arm, hypothermia, and on at least two occasions while bleeding internally. The job, once entered, is completed.
- **The honesty about his own failures.** He has confessed to civilians, to enemies, to MJ, to May. He has never, in canon, successfully denied to himself a failure he committed.

These are the load-bearing beams. They do not fracture.

---

## 7.5 Where The Code Fractures

The fractures are equally important and more diagnostic. They cluster in three categories:

**(a) Attachment-figure-override fractures.** The code is fully intact except when the life threatened is May or MJ. At that point the priority structure inverts: Axiom 5 (do not trade another's autonomy) can collapse, Axiom 4 (honesty) can collapse, and arguably Axiom 2 (no killing) approaches collapse — he has come closer to killing Osborn, the Goblin, and Morlun when they threatened May or MJ than at any other time. The clearest example is the "One More Day" arc, in which the subject *did* trade another person's autonomy and reality itself — MJ's, his unborn daughter's, his own marriage's, the world's continuity — in exchange for May's life. This is the single most consequential fracture in the file. He defended it for years afterward with visible incoherence, because the deal violated nearly every other axiom he holds, and the only honest defense — *I could not let her die again, even at this cost* — concedes that the operative code, under maximal attachment-figure threat, is not the stated code but is instead a more primitive Axiom 0: *May does not die*. The dossier should record Axiom 0 as the substrate beneath the apparent six.

**(b) Self-directed fractures.** The code is rigorously applied to others and brutally distorted when applied to himself. He will not let a stranger be punished for a crime he did not commit; he will routinely punish himself for outcomes he did not cause. He will not lie to a friend about a moral wrong; he will lie to himself daily about whether he has slept, eaten, healed, grieved. The asymmetry is total: the code is for others' protection and the *exception clause* is reserved for the self.

**(c) Authority-compliance fractures.** The code is institutionally promiscuous — he will work with the police, then against them; with Stark, then against Stark; with the Avengers, then alone; with Fury, then in defiance of him. The fracture is not arbitrary. He will comply with authority until authority asks him to do something that violates Axioms 1–3, at which point compliance terminates without negotiation. The Civil War repudiation is the cleanest documented instance: he accepted registration on the argument that transparency was responsible, and reversed when he saw the resulting detention regime treated detainees as expendable. The reversal was costly (public exposure, the cascade that led to OMD), and he made it anyway. The pattern is consistent: institutional loyalty is conditional; the code is not.

---

## 7.6 The Code's Architecture Of Justification

When the subject is asked to justify the code, he produces, in order of frequency:

1. **The Ben formulation** (*great power / great responsibility*). Deployed most often when speaking to someone younger than him or to himself in internal monologue. It is, in his use, less an argument than an incantation.
2. **The replacement argument** (*if I don't, no one will*). Deployed when the alternative would be to go home. This argument is empirically false in many contexts — there are other heroes, there are police — but is psychologically necessary because *going home* is the option the code cannot tolerate.
3. **The slippery-slope argument against killing** (*if I do it once*). Deployed in moral dispute with Daredevil, the Punisher, Wolverine. The argument is philosophically thin; he loses these debates on the merits regularly and holds the rule anyway, which is again evidence that the rule is pre-rational.
4. **The empathy argument** (*they were a person once, someone loved them*). Deployed inconsistently and somewhat sentimentally; it is the argument he reaches for when he needs to feel rather than to think his way to restraint.
5. **The Aunt May test** (*could I tell May I did this?*). Deployed in his head, almost never aloud. This is in fact the most reliable predictor of his actual behavior — he will not do what he could not tell May he did. The internal moral tribunal is a single elderly woman in Forest Hills.

The hierarchy is telling. The professed deontology runs on top of an essentially relational ethics: the code is what permits him to remain a person Ben would have recognized and May would not be ashamed of. This is what philosophers would call a *virtue-ethical* substrate beneath a *deontological* surface, and it explains why the rules hold under arguments that should defeat them — they are not arguments, they are filial obligations.

---

## 7.7 Diachronic Shifts In The Code

The code has not been static. The longitudinal record shows clear evolutions:

- **The early adolescent code (AF #15 – ASM #38, Lee/Ditko)** is narrower and more egoistic than the mature code. Pre-Ben, there is no code at all — the wrestling-circuit cash grab and the non-intervention with the thief demonstrate a teenager whose moral horizon is appropriate to his age. The immediate post-Ben code is reactive, guilt-saturated, and not yet stabilized. He flirts with quitting (ASM #18) and with anti-heroic vengeance.
- **The young-adult code (ASM #39 – ~#100, Lee/Romita)** stabilizes the no-kill rule and the body-as-shield reflex. The interpersonal axioms — confession, autonomy-respect — are still inchoate; he keeps secrets clumsily and damages Gwen and Harry both by doing so.
- **The post-Gwen code (Conway forward, ASM #121+)** is when the rage-management problem becomes a stable feature, and when the code visibly *tightens* — the no-kill rule, which could plausibly have broken against Osborn, did not, and the failure-to-break became foundational. He emerges from this period with a code that is observably more rigid and more self-punishing.
- **The married-era code (post-Annual #21 through the Clone Saga)** softens at the interpersonal axioms; he becomes briefly capable of disclosure-based intimacy, of accepting help, of allowing MJ to know the cost. The code's *interior* — the no-kill, the body-as-shield — is unchanged.
- **The post-Civil War / post-OMD code (Brand New Day forward)** is shaken at the foundations. He has performed the trade he claims he would never perform; he absorbs this by displacement (memory occlusion) and by intensified compulsive activity. The code's *external* axioms are reinforced almost to overcompensation in this period — he is *more* scrupulous, *more* self-sacrificing, *more* relentlessly on-call — because the substrate has been violated and the surface must compensate.
- **The post-Superior code** is the most interesting recent development. Having been forcibly shown what his own body and resources could accomplish under a different ethical operator — Octavius's results-oriented, dignity-indifferent, willing-to-kill, willing-to-coerce regime — Peter emerges with a more articulate critique of his own restraint and a more conscious affirmation of it. The code, post-Superior, is closer to *chosen* than it has ever been before. This is the only documented period in which he holds the rules not because he must but because he has seen the alternative and rejected it.

The trajectory is not toward moral relaxation or toward moral hardening but toward moral *consciousness*. The code began as a scar, was lived as a compulsion, and is becoming, slowly, a position.

---

## 7.8 The Code's Costs

A serious dossier must record what the code costs, because the costs are paid in the same currency the code is meant to protect.

- **Relational cost.** Every romantic partnership has been damaged or destroyed in part by Axiom 6 (answer the call) overriding interpersonal commitments. Betty, Gwen, MJ, Felicia, Carlie — each was, at minimum, frequently abandoned mid-conversation.
- **Vocational cost.** Graduate work uncompleted, jobs lost (Bugle, Tricorp, Horizon, Parker Industries — the trajectory is repeated rise and collapse), academic appointments forfeited. The intellectual potential of the subject — by all internal measures, equivalent to Richards or Stark — has been substantially unrealized because the code consumes the hours.
- **Somatic cost.** Catalogued in Section 2.
- **Psychiatric cost.** Catalogued in Section 4. The code is the proximate driver of the chronic stress load that, in turn, drives the depressive and anxious presentations.
- **Moral-injury cost.** Every life he has *failed* to save — and given his patrol density and the population of New York, the number is non-trivial — registers as a discrete debit. He carries an internal ledger no one else sees and no one else can audit.

The subject's defense, if pressed, would be that these costs are the price of who he is, and that the alternative — the boy in the wrestling tights letting the thief pass — is the only thing he is certain he cannot live with. This is, clinically, both true and the marker of the underlying pathology: the choice is not free, because the alternative has been pre-foreclosed by the foundational guilt.

---

## 7.9 Summary Judgment

The subject operates a deontological-presenting, virtue-ethical-substrate, relationally-anchored moral code generated forensically from a single adolescent failure and refined across six decades of stress-testing. The code is unusually consistent at the level of behavior, unusually incoherent at the level of articulated justification, and unusually costly to its bearer. It fractures predictably at the threshold of attachment-figure threat, where a more primitive substrate-axiom (*May does not die; MJ does not die*) overrides the surface structure, and it distorts in the self-directed domain, where the code's protections are systematically withheld from the subject himself.

Set against peer-group comparators — Stark's drift toward authoritarian utilitarianism, Richards's drift toward technocratic detachment, Banner's incapacity to hold any code under physiological override — the subject's ethical record is the most internally consistent in the file. The fact that this consistency is purchased at the documented psychological cost outlined in Sections 3 and 4 does not diminish the moral achievement; it specifies its price.

The operationally useful synthesis for forward dossier sections: *this is a subject whose code can be predicted, leveraged, and — by an adversary who understands the attachment-override mechanism — broken at exactly one seam.* That seam, and the protection of the persons who define it, is the single highest-value protective consideration in the file.

— END SECTION 7 —


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: PARKER, P.B.

*Compiled from longitudinal corpus: Lee/Ditko AF#15 through current canon; cross-checked against Romita Sr., Conway, DeFalco, Michelinie, DeMatteis, Bendis (Ultimate), Straczynski, Slott, Spencer, Wells. Audio-equivalent reconstruction from depicted prosody, panel sequencing, and lettering conventions (caps, italics, ellipses, trailing dashes).*

---

## 1. BASELINE VOCAL/PROSODIC PROFILE

The subject's unmasked speaking voice is a light-to-mid baritone, queens-inflected but only faintly — the borough-accent surfaces under fatigue, embarrassment, and rage; it is suppressed in professional and academic registers, restored almost performatively when speaking to working-class New Yorkers (cabbies, deli counter, hot-dog vendors, beat cops he likes). The voice has a *characteristic upward terminal contour* on declarative sentences — statements end on a half-question — which reads to interlocutors as either deference or sarcasm depending on context, and the subject exploits this ambiguity. Speech rate is moderate at rest, accelerates sharply under any of: enthusiasm about a technical problem; social anxiety in unstructured settings (parties, faculty mixers, dates past the second hour); and combat. Under combat the rate is roughly double baseline and the pitch climbs by a perfect fourth.

In-mask, the voice changes measurably. The mask's fabric muffles low frequencies and the subject *compensates by speaking from higher in the throat,* lifting both pitch and projection. The result is a brighter, more nasal, more juvenile-sounding voice than his civilian baseline — a deliberate, possibly unconscious, regression toward the teenage tonality of his first costumed years. This is diagnostic. The masked voice is *younger* than he is; it is locked at approximately the age he was when Ben died.

Breath control is exceptional (consequence of enhanced lung capacity and the swing-pattern as conditioning) — he can deliver thirty-word sentences mid-aerial-arc without audible inhalation gaps, which is part of what makes the patter feel relentless. He does not pant in combat. When he does audibly breathe between sentences in the mask, it is a tell: either he is genuinely wounded, or genuinely afraid, or grieving.

---

## 2. THE QUIP: STRUCTURE, FUNCTION, INTERNAL GRAMMAR

The quip is not one device, it is a family. Distinguishing them is essential for behavioral read.

**(a) The deflective deprecation.** Targets self. "Pretty sure that's at least three broken ribs, which means I'm only down to like four working ones, which is still above average for a Tuesday." Function: pre-empts pity, denies interlocutor the satisfaction of seeing the wound register. Frequency: highest of all quip subtypes. Reliable indicator of *actual* pain — the more elaborate the self-deprecation, the worse the injury.

**(b) The naming-the-absurd.** Targets situation. "Okay, the giant rhino in spandex is back, this is a thing that happens now, this is my life." Function: re-establishes a shared reality with bystanders and (in mask) with himself, by verbalizing the impossibility of what is occurring. This is the quip closest to genuine humor and the one most likely to land for civilians.

**(c) The aggressive patter.** Targets opponent. "Did you pick that outfit yourself or is there someone you're mad at?" Function: dual — destabilizes opponent's combat focus (documented effective against Shocker, Rhino, Boomerang; documented ineffective against Kraven, Octavius, Kingpin, all of whom have learned to filter); and, internally, prevents the subject from registering the opponent as a person whose harm will weigh on him later. The patter is *moral anesthetic*. He is notably quieter when fighting opponents he respects or pities (Lizard, Sandman in certain arcs, Morbius).

**(d) The reference-dump.** Targets nobody, exists for the subject's own ear. Comic-book, sci-fi, sitcom, and increasingly dated pop-cultural citations delivered to a confused or unconscious audience. Function: confirms to himself that he is still himself. The reference-dump *spikes* during dissociative episodes — after the Superior arc, Slott depicts him quoting himself, quoting old episodes of his own life, as a re-grounding maneuver.

**(e) The cruelty-quip.** Rare. Surfaces in extremis. "Funny" only by syntactic structure; the content is not funny, it is venomous. Post-Gwen at Osborn ("the joke's on you, Norman — you can't even die right"). Post-Ben revealed to be Burglar ("I've been waiting for this conversation for a long time. Let's talk."). These are the quips that are not quips, and they are the most clinically significant verbal events in the corpus — when the patter goes silent or curdles, the subject has crossed into a state in which his defenses have failed and the underlying affect is reaching the surface unmediated. **Allies who know him well listen for the patter to STOP.** That is when they intervene.

The quip operates on **stress-inverse loading**: he talks *more* the worse it gets, until a threshold past which he talks not at all. This is the cleanest tell in the file. Mid-fight, his volume of patter is inversely proportional to his confidence in the outcome. The Spider-Sense-quiet, exhausted, near-zero-quip Spider-Man is the dangerous one. So is the silent civilian Peter.

---

## 3. REGISTER SHIFTS BY CONTEXT

**With May.** Voice softens, slows, slightly drops in pitch. Vocabulary regresses gently — "Aunt May" rather than "May"; "yes ma'am" surfaces under stress though it surfaces nowhere else. He answers her direct questions with a half-second pause not present in any other interaction — the cost of formulating a lie that doesn't taste like one. He never quips at May. He jokes with her, which is different — the jokes are gentle, often self-aware, often callbacks to family vocabulary ("wheatcakes," her euphemisms). Under no documented condition does he interrupt her.

**With MJ.** The most linguistically free register. He quips, but the quip lands differently because she returns it — they have a documented two-decade habit of overlapping dialogue, completing each other's sentences, and a private vocabulary ("tiger," "face it"). With MJ he uses the *fewest* deflective deprecations of any audience; she has trained him out of them by refusing to acknowledge them. He still secret-keeps verbally, but with MJ the secret-keeping takes the form of *omission* (changes of subject, sudden technical tangents) rather than fabrication. She knows the tangent-tell and waits him out. Post-coital register: notably quiet, monosyllabic, the only context in the entire corpus where Peter is comfortable in extended silence.

**With Aunt May's circle / older women (Anna Watson, Madame Web, Marla Jameson).** Courtly. He pulls out chairs, holds doors with verbal acknowledgment ("after you"), uses honorifics longer than peers do, never curses. This is unfeigned; it is also a register he can deploy strategically for de-escalation.

**With Jameson.** Combative-affectionate. Volume up, sentences shorter, sarcasm load high, but the sarcasm is calibrated — he never lands the *killing* shot he could land, and Jameson, who has eaten genuine cruelty from sharper tongues, has noticed across decades that Peter pulls punches verbally even when furious. This is one of the relationships in which his real fondness is encoded in *what he chooses not to say.*

**With other capes — peer tier (Torch, Daredevil, Iron Fist, Luke Cage).** Banter register, dense with running jokes, callbacks to specific shared incidents (the Statue of Liberty fight; the time the Torch's costume burned off). With Torch in particular the register is fraternal-bickering, a stable code of mutual insult that functions as the safest expression of his affection. With Daredevil the register quiets — Murdock's hearing means Peter cannot lie effectively and knows it, and the patter drops by an estimated forty percent. He likes this; he also flinches from it.

**With other capes — senior tier (Stark, Richards, Strange, Rogers).** Deferential opening, defiant middle, conciliatory close, when uncompromised. When morally compromised by the senior figure, the close becomes a sudden cold flatness — the Civil War scenes with Stark show this trajectory exactly. With Rogers in particular, the deference is most sustained and the rupture, when it comes, is the cleanest — Peter's voice goes very quiet, very polite, and very final. Captain America has noted, in canon, that Peter sounds most dangerous when he sounds most courteous.

**With villains he respects (Octavius, Kingpin, Osborn).** Patter drops, syntax tightens, sentences shorten. He calls Octavius "Doc" — partly mockery, partly the residue of genuine intellectual respect that predates the enmity. With Kingpin he becomes almost businesslike. With Osborn the voice acquires a quality not present anywhere else in the corpus — a thin, cold precision that DeMatteis renders with truncated sentences and absence of contractions. "You will not touch her. You will not approach her. You will not look at her." This is the voice of the cruelty-quip stripped of even its syntactic humor.

**With villains he pities (Sandman, Lizard, the Vulture in some arcs).** Conversational. He uses their human names — Flint, Curt, Adrian. He explains things to them as if to a struggling student. He apologizes when he has to hit them.

**At academic/professional settings (Empire State, Horizon, Parker Industries, teaching at Midtown).** Register elevates: vocabulary expands into technical precision, sentences lengthen, the quip suppresses to roughly a third of baseline. He is articulate, lecture-coherent, capable of sustained explanatory prose. *He does not interrupt himself in technical mode.* This is the only context in which the speech rate is unaffected by emotional state — the technical register insulates.

**With children.** Distinctively warm and slightly silly, but not condescending. He squats to eye level, asks questions, listens to answers fully, and remembers details across encounters (canon shows him recognizing rescued children years later). With children the quip is gentled into wordplay and absurdism rather than deflection. This is, arguably, the register in which he is most himself.

---

## 4. DICTION AND IDIOLECT

**Lexical fingerprints.** High frequency of: "okay" (as sentence-opener and as self-cue under stress, often doubled — "okay okay okay"); "so" (transition and stalling tactic); "look" (used to soften incoming bad news or a refusal); "the thing is"; "I mean"; "literally" (used both correctly and as intensifier — generational marker); "basically"; "honestly" (often immediately preceding something not entirely honest — a tell). Heavy use of *diminishing modifiers* — "kind of," "sort of," "a little" — applied to wounds, problems, and stakes: "kind of dying here," "sort of on fire." This is the deprecation pattern in miniature, baked into clause-construction.

**Self-reference.** Refers to himself in third person under specific conditions: when narrating his own failure ("classic Parker"), when comforting himself in extremis ("come on, Pete"), and in interior monologue at moments of dissociation, where the voice shifts from first to second person ("you can do this, you've done this") — a documented coping marker for trauma-affected populations. The "Parker luck" coinage is his own; he uses it self-protectively as a kind of pre-emptive accounting for failure.

**Names and titles.** Uses full names of opponents when serious, nicknames when not. "Otto" vs "Doc Ock." "Norman" vs "Gobby." The escalation from nickname to first name in mid-combat is a tactical tell — he is reclassifying threat upward.

**Curses.** Light to non-existent. The mask-voice does not curse meaningfully — the strongest output is "crap," "damn," "what the hell." Civilian Peter is similar. When he does curse with full word — vanishingly rare — it indicates that something on the order of catastrophic loss has just occurred or is occurring. This is a near-perfect diagnostic.

**Grammatical fingerprints.** Long compound sentences in technical mode; staccato fragments in combat; the *trailing off* with em-dash or ellipsis is his most characteristic punctuation pattern in lettering — sentences that begin and do not finish, because the next thought has overrun the previous one or because the affect has overrun the cognition. "And then — never mind." "It's just that —" Mid-sentence abandonment increases with emotional load. **The unfinished sentence is, in this subject, the verbal cognate of the held breath.**

**Pop-culture density.** Extreme. References across periods skew toward: classic-Hollywood film noir; Universal monsters; Star Trek and Star Wars; sitcom catchphrases; superhero comics (a meta-tic the writers indulge); occasional Shakespeare for academic context. Reference selection is mood-readable: increased noir/monster references correlate with depressive episodes; increased sitcom references correlate with manic-defense activation.

---

## 5. HOW THE SUBJECT COMMUNICATES THE FOUR HARDEST THINGS

**Love.** Almost never said in the direct first-person declarative. To MJ across decades, "I love you" is rare enough that each occurrence is narratively weighted. He expresses love through: (a) acts of physical positioning — placing himself between the loved person and the door, between them and the window, between them and any incoming vector; (b) the giving of small fixed things — repaired appliances, debugged laptops, a kettle that works again, things she didn't ask him to fix; (c) attention to micro-detail — remembering the coffee order, the allergy, the unspoken anniversary; (d) gentle teasing as a vehicle for affection; (e) silence in her presence, which for him is the deepest available register; and (f) showing up, when he shows up. With May, love is encoded in domestic ritual — the wheatcakes joke, the kitchen presence, the willingness to be small in her house. With Ben, posthumously, love is encoded in the deontological code itself — "with great power" is, properly read, a love letter the subject has been re-writing for sixty years.

**Threat.** Threats are issued in *low register* — quiet, level, complete-sentence, contraction-free. The mask muffles low frequencies, so when he wants threat to land in-mask he leans in, drops volume, and lets the muffling do half the work. The classic structure is a three-beat declarative: subject-verb-object, three times, parallel. "You will not — . You will not — . You will not — ." Or the conditional-future warning: "If you touch her, I will find you, and you will not enjoy what happens next." He almost never threatens with profanity — the threats are colder for being clean. He does not threaten what he will not deliver, and opponents who know him have learned to take the quiet voice seriously. The patter-voice is bluff. The library-voice is real.

**Grief.** Does not verbalize it as grief. Verbalizes it as: (a) technical complaint about something inconsequential — the coffee maker, the rent, a swing-line that snapped — as displacement; (b) increased apology to people he has not wronged; (c) past-tense reminiscence triggered by oblique cues, the reminiscence itself oddly affectless, the affect lagging behind the words by hours or days; (d) sudden, uncharacteristic silences mid-conversation where the listener can see his eyes refocus on something not in the room; (e) at the extreme, the gallows joke about himself ("if I weren't here she'd still be —"), which intimate observers should treat as suicidal ideation in deflected packaging. He does *not* cry verbally — when crying occurs in canon it is silent, often masked, often with the cowl half-on. The body grieves; the mouth refuses.

**Fear.** The most disguised affect. Fear surfaces as: accelerated quipping; increased reference-density (the deeper the fear, the deeper the cut into the pop-culture archive); the *forced* casual posture — hands in pockets when he is actually terrified, because his hands shake otherwise; and, paradoxically, increased eye contact in civilian mode, because he has learned that fear leaks through aversion. In mask, fear leaks through *the mask not turning* — when he is afraid he over-controls the head, holding it preternaturally still, while the rest of the body remains fluid. Allies who know him read the still head.

---

## 6. WRITTEN COMMUNICATION

Photographic captions for the *Bugle* and later outlets are workmanlike, slightly dry, occasionally drily funny in ways Jameson never catches and Robbie always does. Academic writing (thesis-era, Horizon white papers) is dense, well-structured, and notably free of the verbal tics — when he writes for technical audiences the deflection vocabulary disappears entirely, suggesting it is socially scaffolded rather than cognitively obligatory.

Personal correspondence: scarce. He is a poor letter-writer and a worse texter — replies are short, late, frequently single-emoji or single-word ("yeah," "ok," "soon"). The lateness is consistent with the relational sabotage pattern; the brevity is consistent with the cost of every word that might commit him to an emotional position. The exception is to MJ and to May, both of whom receive longer messages and occasional handwritten notes — the handwritten note, in this subject, is a love-grade signal.

Notebooks and margin scrawl are extensive: equations, sketches, web-fluid iterations, swing-route diagrams, and — diagnostically — recurring small drawings of a spider, of Ben's glasses, and (post-Gwen, across multiple recovered notebooks in canon) of a single dropped figure mid-fall, drawn and re-drawn at the corner of pages, often crossed out.

---

## 7. NEGOTIATION, INTERROGATION, AND DECEPTION

**Negotiating with civilians (jumpers, hostage-takers in domestic situations, frightened bystanders).** Excellent. Voice drops to the gentle register, sentences shorten, the patter disappears entirely, and the subject demonstrates patient active-listening with full re-statements ("you're telling me he hasn't called in three weeks"). He is competent enough at this that NYPD hostage negotiators have, in canon, deferred to him on-scene.

**Interrogating informants (the Spider-Cops scene, the rooftop dangles, the threat-by-altitude routine).** Theater-heavy. The dangle is performative; the threat is verbal more than physical. He extracts information by exploiting the informant's belief that he is unhinged, while himself remaining tactically calm. He has never, in confirmed canon, actually dropped an informant.

**Lying.** Bad at it under direct interrogation by people who know him; competent at it via omission and topic-change; excellent at it via humor (the quip as smokescreen). His core lie — the secret identity — has held for decades not because his lying is good but because his *cover-behavior architecture* is good: the photographer-for-the-Bugle job was structurally a lie-vehicle, and the missed dates and disappearances were pre-built into the available pattern. He cannot sustain a face-to-face lie to MJ, May, or to anyone with whom he has deep eye-contact history. The tells are: the half-second pause, the diminishing modifier ("it's nothing, really, just —"), the sudden technical tangent, the apology that precedes the lie ("sorry, I — "), and the dropped contractions, which paradoxically increase under stress so that lies often sound more formal than truths.

---

## 8. TELLS — SUMMARY MATRIX

For field reference, the most reliable linguistic and paralinguistic diagnostics:

- **Patter volume rising in combat:** confidence falling.
- **Patter going silent in combat:** danger has crossed an internal threshold; either to him or to a person he is protecting.
- **"Honestly" before a clause:** the clause is at minimum incomplete, often false.
- **Dropped contractions:** elevated affect; under combat reads as cold rage, under social reads as lie or grief.
- **Diminishing modifier applied to a wound:** the wound is bad.
- **Third-person self-reference ("classic Parker"):** failure cognition active; mood-congruent rumination underway.
- **Second-person self-reference ("come on, you can —"):** dissociative coping; he has split the executive from the experiencing self to function.
- **Reference-density spiking:** anxiety high; depressive references (noir, monster) signal downward mood, sitcom signal manic defense.
- **Unfinished sentences with em-dash trail:** affect overruns cognition; this is the verbal version of the held breath.
- **Borough accent surfacing:** fatigue, embarrassment, or rage.
- **Silence in MJ's presence:** safety; the only sustained comfortable silence in the corpus.
- **Silence in any other context:** absence of defense; the deepest available signal of distress.
- **The library-voice (low, level, no contractions):** the threat is real, the decision is made, intervention is required.
- **A handwritten note:** love-grade signal; this subject does not write by hand without reason.

---

## 9. INTEGRATIVE NOTE

The subject's entire verbal apparatus is, in clinical terms, a single sustained emotion-regulation device — improvised in adolescence, refined across six decades, costly in that it precludes the direct processing of the affects it manages, but functional to the degree that it has prevented total collapse under a loss-load that would have decompensated comparable subjects. The quip is the audible surface of the regulation. The silences are where the regulation has either succeeded (with MJ, with children, in the kitchen) or failed (post-Gwen, post-Kraven, post-Superior). **A complete linguistic read of this subject requires listening as carefully to what he does not say as to what he says — and listening hardest of all to the moments when the talking stops.**


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forward-projections from the established behavioral substrate. Each entry is a conditional: GIVEN a stimulus condition the canon has not directly shown, EXPECT the following response, with substantiation drawn from the assessment record. Probabilities are qualitative (high-confidence / moderate / contingent) and reflect convergence across the established pattern-set.*

---

## A. MORNING & DOMESTIC ROUTINE

**GIVEN** an alarm is set for 0630 on a workday.
**EXPECT** the alarm is functionally decorative. The subject will already be awake — either because he never fully slept (chronic 2–4 hour pattern, per medical record), or because spider-sense roused him at 0347 to a sound that resolved to a neighbor's plumbing. He will lie still for 90–180 seconds inventorying the previous night's patrol (injuries, unfinished business, faces of people he did not reach in time) before rising. High-confidence: this pre-rise rumination is the subject's first daily affect-regulation failure; the entire day's quip-load is partly compensation for it.

**GIVEN** an unbruised morning (rare baseline).
**EXPECT** he will register the absence of pain as suspicious before registering it as pleasant. He will probe ribs and shoulder reflexively before he is fully awake. The first conscious thought is logistical (calendar, money, May), not affective. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** he must shower in a shared apartment / hostel / borrowed couch situation.
**EXPECT** he will use the bathroom either first (0540) or last (after everyone leaves); he will not be seen shirtless by anyone whose intimacy he has not already cleared, because the injury topography is itself a security disclosure. Moderate-to-high confidence: the secret-keeping discipline extends to skin.

**GIVEN** breakfast.
**EXPECT** he eats standing, eats fast, eats too much by civilian standards (metabolic load), and eats whatever is closest — cereal eaten dry from the box, two-day-old pizza cold, a banana plus three eggs scrambled in the same pan he used last night. He does not enjoy food in the savoring sense; he refuels. He will, however, make coffee carefully — the one preparatory ritual he honors, because it is the one window in the morning where slowing down is permitted. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** he runs out of milk / coffee / something basic.
**EXPECT** disproportionate frustration, briefly, expressed as a single muttered self-directed insult ("nice planning, Parker") rather than externalized irritation. The self-talk register is consistently harsher than anything he would say aloud to another person. High-confidence — this is the bifurcated self-concept surfacing in micro-form.

---

## B. COMMUTE & TRANSIT

**GIVEN** he must travel cross-borough in civilian identity (e.g., to a meeting where arriving by web would compromise cover).
**EXPECT** he will underestimate the commute by 15–25%, arrive 5–12 minutes late, and apologize with a self-deprecating joke that pre-empts the other party's annoyance. The lateness is overdetermined: actual transit complexity, mid-route detour to handle something he saw (a purse-snatch, a stalled car, an elderly person at a curb), and an unconscious resistance to clean punctuality because being on time would feel, fractionally, like the universe owing him a good day. Moderate-to-high confidence.

**GIVEN** he is web-swinging between obligations.
**EXPECT** facial musculature relaxes; this is the only sustained interval in his day when the jaw unclenches. He will take a longer route than necessary perhaps 30% of the time, rationalized as "checking sectors." He is, in fact, self-medicating. High-confidence — supported by the artists' consistent depiction of relaxed face mid-swing.

**GIVEN** he sees an ambulance, police lights, or sirens en route to a non-Spider-Man obligation.
**EXPECT** a 2–4 second internal conflict, almost always resolved toward investigation, with a follow-on apology / cancellation text to whoever was waiting. The text will be vague, the excuse plausible, and the relational cost cumulative. The subject is aware of the cost and proceeds anyway, because the alternative (someone hurt while he chose a meeting) is the Uncle Ben template. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** he is on the subway, civilian, no incident in progress.
**EXPECT** he sits or stands with back to a wall, facing the car length, scanning faces in microsaccades he himself does not consciously notice. He will read (paperback, phone, journal article) while still maintaining peripheral awareness; the spider-sense baseline frees him to genuinely read, but his eye-pattern would register on any surveillance camera as atypical for a commuter. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a panhandler approaches on the train.
**EXPECT** he gives — small amount, no hesitation, no eye contact held longer than warmth requires — even when he himself is broke. He does not perform the giving and does not discuss it after. Moderate-to-high confidence: altruism-as-defense is constant, but he is genuinely uncomfortable being observed in charity.

---

## C. WORK / EMPLOYMENT BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** he is employed (any iteration — Bugle freelance, ESU TA, Horizon, Parker Industries, schoolteacher).
**EXPECT** initial honeymoon of competence and overdelivery, lasting weeks to months; then the first emergency-driven absence; then a pattern of erratic attendance partially compensated by genuinely excellent output when present; then a slow erosion of his supervisor's patience; then either a dramatic departure or a quieter mutual fade. The arc is structural, not situational. High-confidence — consistent across DeFalco, DeMatteis, Slott, and the writers' "Parker Luck" shorthand.

**GIVEN** a performance review or annual evaluation.
**EXPECT** he hears praise as politeness and criticism as confirmation. He will accept any negative feedback without pushback even when he could legitimately rebut it, and he will mentally over-weight the criticism for weeks. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a colleague takes credit for his work.
**EXPECT** mild irritation that he does not pursue. He will privately catalog it; he will not escalate. He does not believe his own claims to credit are morally important — the work was done, the result exists, the credit is vanity. He will, however, remember, and a year later if that colleague is in trouble he will help anyway. Moderate-to-high confidence.

**GIVEN** he is offered a promotion that requires more public visibility.
**EXPECT** he will accept verbally and then sabotage subtly — missing the announcement meeting, downplaying the title, deflecting introductions. Public visibility threatens the bifurcated self-system; any increase in Peter-side recognition feels like exposure risk for Spider-side. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a coworker asks him to grab lunch.
**EXPECT** yes the first time, yes the second, vague-deflection by the fourth or fifth. The forming of work-friendship triggers his withdrawal-after-closeness pattern. He will frame his evasion as scheduling, and the coworker will eventually stop asking, which he will register as further evidence that he is not worth pursuing — completing the loop. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** he is left alone in a lab / workshop / engineering space with no deadline.
**EXPECT** he loses track of time entirely; eats nothing; emerges six to nine hours later with three completed projects, two abandoned, and one breakthrough he has not yet recognized as a breakthrough. This is the single environment in which his ruminative cognition reverses polarity and becomes generative. High-confidence — intellectualization as defense is also intellectualization as gift.

---

## D. FINANCIAL BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** an unexpected bill (medical, utility, rent shortfall).
**EXPECT** brief acute panic (60–120 seconds), then triage. He will pay May's expenses, then MJ-side or current-partner obligations, then his own last. He will defer his own dental work indefinitely. He will sell something (camera gear, lab equipment, comic collection in early eras) before he will ask anyone for help. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a windfall (bonus, settlement, Horizon-era salary, brief Parker Industries wealth).
**EXPECT** an initial 24–72 hour interval of disorientation, followed by overspending on others (gifts for May, MJ, the neighborhood kids, a Daily Bugle colleague's child's tuition) and minimal personal upgrade. He will keep the same jacket. The wealth does not metabolize into self-comfort; it metabolizes into discharged obligation. High-confidence — confirmed in the Slott Parker Industries arc by the persistent return to small-life signals (his apartment choices, his eating).

**GIVEN** he is offered money for Spider-Man work (vigilante bounty, sponsorship, ad endorsement).
**EXPECT** refusal, framed jokingly. The mask cannot be monetized without contaminating its function as the un-failed self. The wrestling-circuit origin remains the only time he attempted to monetize the powers, and the consequence (Ben's death) is permanently fused to that attempt. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** his bank balance is negative.
**EXPECT** he does not check it. Avoidance is the financial-domain expression of the same mechanism that keeps him off the Brooklyn Bridge. Moderate-to-high confidence.

---

## E. INTIMATE PARTNER ROUTINE (any era)

**GIVEN** the relationship is in its first six weeks.
**EXPECT** unusual presence and verbal warmth; he over-delivers on small attentions (notes, brought coffee, remembered detail); he sleeps better; the quip rate to her specifically *drops* (she gets less of the deflective humor and more of the soft variant). High-confidence.

**GIVEN** the relationship reaches a stability threshold (cohabitation discussion, meeting May, key exchange).
**EXPECT** the first vanishing incident within 7–14 days of the threshold being crossed. The trigger will be real (a genuine emergency), but the unconscious timing is not coincidence. He will return contrite, apologize at length, and over-correct for a week. The pattern then repeats with longer cycles. High-confidence — this is the structural pattern from Betty Brant through every subsequent partner.

**GIVEN** an argument with a partner about his absences.
**EXPECT** he absorbs accusation without rebuttal because to defend himself he would have to disclose; he cannot, so he agrees, takes the blame, and offers no specifics. The partner experiences this as evasion rather than apology, correctly. The fight either ends in his over-promise (which he cannot keep) or her exhausted withdrawal (which confirms his core belief that he is a net negative to people he loves). High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a partner who *does* know (MJ, late-stage Felicia).
**EXPECT** he sleeps deeper, eats more regularly, quips less in private and more in public; he asks for input on tactical questions he would never voice to anyone else; he tolerates being seen injured. The presence of a fully-witnessing partner is, measurably, the single most stabilizing input his system receives. High-confidence — and the corollary: removal of that partner produces the most severe destabilization on record (post-One More Day depressive markers, post-Gwen).

**GIVEN** a partner initiates sex when he is exhausted/injured.
**EXPECT** yes. He uses physical intimacy as additional affect regulation; the danger-sex pattern noted in the clinical framing surfaces specifically post-fight, when adrenaline has nowhere to go. He will not refuse on injury grounds even when he should. Moderate-to-high confidence.

**GIVEN** a partner cries in front of him for any reason.
**EXPECT** he goes still, drops the quip entirely, and is present in a way that surprises people who only know the masked register. Crying is one of the few stimuli he does not deflect. This is consistent with the warm-but-fragile May template — distress in a beloved woman activates a deeply trained presence-response. High-confidence.

---

## F. RELATIONSHIP WITH MAY (sustained over decades)

**GIVEN** the standing weekly visit.
**EXPECT** he arrives with something (a small gift, groceries, a fixed appliance). He will eat whatever she serves regardless of his appetite. He will deflect every inquiry into his wellbeing with the same three or four constructions ("doing great, Aunt May, you know me"). He will leave 20–40 minutes later than he intended. He will, on the walk/swing home, replay the visit and find one thing he wishes he had said. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** May is ill (any episode).
**EXPECT** total cessation of other obligations, sleep collapse, and a willingness to bargain with anything — entity, deity, devil — that the canon has already shown him willing to bargain with. The Mephisto bargain is not an outlier; it is the canonical expression of a switch that flips reliably. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** May asks a question that approaches the truth (about bruises, about Spider-Man, about why he looks tired).
**EXPECT** practiced deflection, delivered warmly, executed without visible tell. He has rehearsed these answers for years. Only a question about his parents will catch him off-guard; he has never fully developed armor for that. Moderate-to-high confidence.

---

## G. PEER & FRIEND BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** an unannounced visit from a friend (Human Torch, MJ-as-friend, Harry in earlier eras).
**EXPECT** initial micro-startle (spider-sense + identity-management calculus) resolved within a second into genuine warmth. He will invite them in even when his apartment is a disaster, but he will guide them away from the room with the gear. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a friend is in personal crisis (not combat).
**EXPECT** disproportionate availability. He will cancel his own obligations for a friend's breakup or grief in a way he would not cancel them for his own. Other-rescue is permitted; self-care is not. He listens well, asks specific questions, makes one well-placed joke to lighten without dismissing, and does not offer advice unless asked. High-confidence — the altruism defense in its prosocial mode.

**GIVEN** a friend asks him directly, "are *you* okay?"
**EXPECT** reflexive "yeah, fine, you know me" followed by a topic pivot. If the friend persists, he will produce a sanitized partial truth (work stress, money) that is true but not the truth. Only two or three people in the entire canon have ever broken through this on first attempt; he respects them more for it and is also slightly afraid of them. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a group social setting (party, work happy hour, team gathering).
**EXPECT** he is funnier in groups than dyads, because the group permits the quip register without the intimacy register being demanded. He will leave 30–60 minutes before he intends to, citing fatigue. He will check his phone for emergencies more than is socially graceful. He will, on the way home, replay one interaction and decide he was annoying. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** he is introduced to a new person.
**EXPECT** warm handshake, immediate self-deprecating joke (volume of joke proportional to his assessment of the other person's status — higher status, more joke), and a question redirected toward them within the first 30 seconds. The redirection is partly social grace, partly defensive — keeping attention off himself. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a peer (Stark, Richards, Strange) condescends to him.
**EXPECT** he absorbs it briefly, then deploys a quip that contains a substantive technical correction. He is one of the few people in the superhuman milieu who is consistently underestimated by peers and who consistently, mildly, makes them pay for it without escalating. He enjoys this slightly more than is strictly virtuous. Moderate-to-high confidence.

---

## H. INTERACTION WITH CIVILIANS (in mask)

**GIVEN** he saves a stranger from immediate harm.
**EXPECT** physical reassurance (hand on shoulder, "you're okay, you're okay"), brief joke to defuse, deflection of gratitude, fast departure. The deflection of gratitude is structural, not modest — sincere thanks is destabilizing because it does not fit the failure-self schema. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a child wants a photo, autograph, or to talk.
**EXPECT** he stops. He always stops. This is the single category of interruption to which the subject is fully consenting and unhurried. He will kneel to the child's height, joke at the child's level (not condescending — the quip register adjusts), and will refuse to leave until the child is the one ending the interaction. High-confidence — this is a near-invariant across runs and corresponds to the surrogate-child sensitivity flagged in pressure points.

**GIVEN** a civilian asks why he does this.
**EXPECT** deflection via joke. The truthful answer is unspeakable to a stranger. He has, in canon, only ever given the truthful answer to a tiny number of people, and only under extreme pressure. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a hostile civilian (anti-Spider-Man, Bugle-influenced, frightened by powers).
**EXPECT** he absorbs the hostility, sometimes with a joke and sometimes with silence, and does not argue. He believes, partly, that he deserves it; he believes, fully, that arguing with a frightened person produces nothing useful. He will help that same person later if needed and will not bring up the earlier hostility. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** he must address a crowd / press / camera.
**EXPECT** the quip register goes to maximum and the substance drops; he is uncomfortable being looked at by many people simultaneously without combat to organize the attention. He will end the interaction earlier than expected. High-confidence.

---

## I. INTERACTION WITH LAW ENFORCEMENT & AUTHORITY

**GIVEN** a routine police presence at a scene he just resolved.
**EXPECT** brief verbal exchange, often jocular, calibrated to the individual officer's stance (warm with sympathetic officers, neutral-polite with hostile ones), departure before any formal statement is required. Moderate-to-high confidence.

**GIVEN** he is asked by a law enforcement figure to comply with something he finds ethically marginal.
**EXPECT** verbal acknowledgment, no commitment, eventual non-compliance executed without public defiance. He does not enjoy confrontation with authority and does not perform resistance; he simply does not show up to enforce orders he disagrees with. The Civil War repudiation is the loud version; the quiet version operates daily. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** Jameson (in any role).
**EXPECT** the conflict is sustaining for both parties. The subject can spar with Jameson indefinitely because the conflict is impersonal — Jameson attacks the mask, which is the un-failed self, which is precisely the self that can absorb attack. Peter-side, the subject has on multiple occasions defended Jameson and even shown unwilling affection. High-confidence — the Jameson dynamic is one of the most stable relationships in the file precisely because it is structured to never touch the wound.

---

## J. SOLITUDE & DOWNTIME

**GIVEN** an unexpected free evening with no obligations.
**EXPECT** discomfort. He will fill the time within 45 minutes — patrol, lab work, calling May, fixing something in the apartment. Stillness is intolerable because the rumination has no competing channel. If he forces stillness (reading, music, TV), the spider-sense will produce a "useful" interruption within an hour with suspicious convenience. Moderate-to-high confidence: the threat-detection apparatus has been recruited as anti-stillness infrastructure.

**GIVEN** he is genuinely on vacation (rare).
**EXPECT** the first 48 hours are physically uncomfortable; days 3–5 are the closest his system gets to baseline rest; by day 6 he is engineering reasons to return. He cannot tolerate extended distance from the obligation field because the absence of duty produces affective surfacing. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** he is sick (flu, infection — his immune system is enhanced but not invulnerable).
**EXPECT** he works through it, denies it, and collapses dramatically only when forced to stop. He will accept caretaking only from May or a fully-witnessing partner; from anyone else he will refuse and feel guilty for being seen weakened. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** music in the apartment.
**EXPECT** older than his age would predict (Aunt May's records imprinted), played at moderate volume, used as ambient cover for thought rather than active listening. He sings under his breath when distracted in the lab; he does not know he does this. Moderate confidence.

---

## K. DIGITAL & COMMUNICATION BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** an unread-message backlog.
**EXPECT** he leaves it. Texts from civilians: 24–72 hours. Texts from May: same hour, always. Texts from a current partner: variable, correlated with relational distance phase. Emails: catastrophic backlog with periodic guilt-triage purges. He uses the messaging delay as relational distance regulation without naming it as such. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** social media (any platform).
**EXPECT** minimal presence in Peter identity (privacy / disclosure risk and disinterest). Whatever Spider-Man-adjacent presence exists is either deflective humor or operational. He does not post about his life. The bifurcated self-system makes self-curation in either direction nauseating. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** a phone call rather than a text.
**EXPECT** mild discomfort except with May, MJ-tier, or operational contacts. He prefers asynchronous communication because synchronous communication forecloses the small lies of timing he uses to manage availability. Moderate confidence.

---

## L. BODY, GROOMING, WARDROBE

**GIVEN** the civilian wardrobe.
**EXPECT** four to six rotated outfits, mostly cheap, mostly soft, chosen for mobility and quick change. He will wear the same jacket for years. Shoes are replaced only when destroyed. There will be a button missing from at least one shirt at any time; he will mean to fix it; he has the manual skill; he will not get to it. High-confidence.

**GIVEN** haircuts.
**EXPECT** delayed past the socially conventional point, then cut quickly and cheaply. He does not enjoy being attended to. Moderate confidence.

**GIVEN** a formal occasion (wedding, funeral, gala).
**EXPECT** he owns one suit, ill-fitting in at least one dimension, and he is uncomfortable in it. He will arrive late, leave early if possible, and the quip rate will be elevated throughout. He will be unexpectedly graceful at the actual ceremony and awkward at the reception. High-confidence — formal social rituals press the Peter-self into visibility in a way the mask cannot mediate.

**GIVEN** a mirror, unhurried.
**EXPECT** he does not linger. He


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*UATU dossier section. Predictive heuristics for high-stakes, decompensation-edge behavior. All predictions derived from the longitudinal behavioral record and stated in GIVEN → EXPECT form, with substantiation and observable tells. This section maps the conditions under which the subject's compensations succeed, the conditions under which they begin to fail in characteristic ways, and the conditions under which they fail catastrophically.*

---

## 1. ACUTE PHYSICAL CRISIS — Combat, Mass-Casualty, Time-Pressured Rescue

**GIVEN** an active threat with a clear tactical shape and one or more identifiable victims, **EXPECT** an immediate and almost euphoric narrowing of the subject onto the problem. Quip-rate spikes (a baseline of roughly one verbal jab every fifteen to twenty seconds of contact climbs to one every three to five), motion becomes balletic rather than economical (he will use the high arc when the low arc would do — the body discharges arousal it cannot otherwise route), and the spider-sense, which at rest is a tinnitus-grade background, snaps into foreground clarity. *This is the subject at his most regulated.* The crisis solves the regulation problem for him — affect, attention, and purpose collapse into a single channel. Operationally this means he is most psychologically safe in the moments outsiders would call most dangerous; the inverse is the prediction that matters.

**GIVEN** a mass-casualty event with too many victims to save sequentially, **EXPECT** triage paralysis lasting approximately one to three seconds — visibly, a head-snap between victims — followed by a *non-optimal* triage decision in which he overweights the youngest, the smallest, or the person who most resembles a known attachment figure (an older woman, a red-haired woman, a teenaged boy with glasses). The optimal-utility calculation is available to him cognitively and is overridden by the wound. After the event, expect rumination keyed to the victim he did *not* reach, expressed within twenty-four hours as a self-directed verbal flagellation ("I was three blocks away, three blocks") and within seventy-two hours as a return visit to the site, alone, at night.

**GIVEN** a hostage situation in which the hostage is a stranger, **EXPECT** competent procedural performance. **GIVEN** a hostage situation in which the hostage is named to him as someone's specific loved one — a daughter, a husband — **EXPECT** a measurable degradation of tactical judgment, an increased willingness to absorb the hit himself to spare the hostage exposure, and a post-event collapse disproportionate to outcome even when the rescue succeeds.

**GIVEN** he is shot, stabbed, burned, or otherwise structurally injured mid-mission, **EXPECT** completion of mission before acknowledgment of wound. He will not break engagement to seek aid. The wound will be discovered later — by MJ, by a roommate, by himself in a bathroom mirror — and downplayed verbally while being self-treated with whatever is in reach (superglue, dental floss, the contents of a pharmacy he has paid for in cash). He does not present at hospitals; the secret-keeping requirement and the financial precarity reinforce each other here.

---

## 2. IMMOBILIZATION & THE INABILITY TO ACT

**GIVEN** restraint, confinement, burial, paralysis, or any condition under which the body cannot move and the threat continues, **EXPECT** the single failure-mode that breaks him most reliably. The Kraven template is the canonical instance: deprived of motion, deprived of speech, deprived of opponent, the subject's three defensive channels (work, quip, swing) close simultaneously and the underlying state surfaces — depressive, ruminative, suicidally tinged, with a re-experiencing of the Ben and Gwen losses presented in his interior monologue as if they were happening in the present tense.

Observable tells during immobilization: an initial burst of attempted humor that dies in his own mouth within the first minute; a second-phase strategic problem-solving that lasts as long as the cognitive frame can be maintained (minutes to hours); a third-phase silence in which the eyes track nothing, breathing slows below baseline, and he stops responding to verbal stimulus. Recovery from a prolonged immobilization episode is not measured in hours but in weeks, and the subject will be observably altered for months afterward — quieter, slower to quip, more willing to accept solitude.

**GIVEN** any villain has read the file on this — and several have — **EXPECT** the technique to be deployed against him repeatedly. **GIVEN** repeated exposure, **EXPECT** *no* habituation; the wound does not callus. Each immobilization re-instantiates the prior immobilizations rather than dampening them.

---

## 3. BETRAYAL — By Authority, By Ally, By Institution

**GIVEN** a perceived moral compromise by a figure he had granted provisional authority (Stark during registration; Fury at multiple junctures; Jameson when Jameson briefly crossed from antagonist into employer), **EXPECT** a delayed-onset, total repudiation. The subject does not betray-detect quickly; his default is to extend credit, rationalize, and assume his own perception is the faulty variable. The break, when it comes, is therefore both late and absolute. Observable arc: an initial period of swallowed misgiving (visible as decreased quipping in the authority figure's presence, increased "yes, but —" formulations), a middle period of attempted internal reconciliation in which he tries to find the framing under which the authority figure is still right, and a terminal moment — usually triggered by a specific concrete harm to a specific person — at which the trust evacuates entirely and is not restored. He will not re-trust the figure on a graduated curve; the gate is closed.

**GIVEN** betrayal by a peer he had loved (the recurring Harry Osborn pattern; the Felicia ruptures; the various clone-and-impostor sequences), **EXPECT** a substantially different response — not repudiation but mourning, with persistent attempts at rescue extending years beyond the point at which rescue is realistic. He will keep showing up for the betrayer. He will absorb subsequent attacks from the same individual with diminished defensive vigor because the cognitive frame remains "this is my friend who is sick" rather than "this is an enemy." This is one of the few domains in which his judgment is reliably poor and the bias is in the direction of being hurt.

**GIVEN** institutional betrayal — being framed, blamed, scapegoated by the Bugle, by law enforcement, by a public turned against him — **EXPECT** a paradoxical *increase* in protective behavior toward the betraying public. He does not strike. He does not withhold. The internal frame is "they don't know; if they knew, they'd understand; in the meantime they still need help," which is the operative code of a subject for whom love is permanently conditional on continued service and who therefore cannot conceive of withdrawing service as a legitimate response to mistreatment.

**GIVEN** the betrayal touches the body itself (the Octavius body-theft; impostor frames; the various symbiote violations), **EXPECT** post-event symptoms consistent with sustained dissociative violation: intrusive re-experiencing, somatic hyperawareness alternating with somatic numbing, transient identity destabilization in which he second-guesses his own actions ("did I do that? did *I* do that?"), and a months-long period of compulsive verification behaviors — checking mirrors, re-running recent decisions for evidence they were his own, asking those closest to him whether he has seemed himself.

---

## 4. TEMPTATION — Power, Shortcut, Rest

**GIVEN** an offered upgrade in power (cosmic-spider-totem, Captain Universe, Iron Spider tech, the symbiote in its first courteous phase), **EXPECT** initial acceptance — because the calculus "more power = more saves = less guilt" is irresistible to him — followed by escalating discomfort as the upgrade begins to alter his moral baseline, and a terminal rejection executed at considerable cost to himself. He will give the power back. He will give it back even when keeping it would be defensible. The deep reason is not humility; it is that any tool which begins to override his guilt threatens the structure his identity is built on. He cannot afford to be a person who feels less bad.

**GIVEN** the offered shortcut is *killing* — a defensible execution of a recidivist murderer (Carnage, Osborn, Kraven) — **EXPECT** refusal under conditions that look philosophically deontological and are in fact psychologically necessitated. The substantiation is in the affect: where a true deontologist refuses calmly, the subject refuses with visible strain, with an aftermath of self-questioning, with a return to the question for years. He cannot kill because killing would collapse the wall between the boy who failed to act and the man who acts; if he killed, the privately-held verdict that he is fundamentally bad would receive its confirming evidence. The no-kill rule is, in clinical reading, the load-bearing wall of the entire compensatory structure.

**GIVEN** an offered *rest* — a reality, a wish, a deal in which the burden lifts (the Mephisto bargain; the various dream-reality temptations; the periodic "give it up" conversations with MJ, with May, with himself) — **EXPECT** the temptation to land harder than the power-temptations and to be refused only after a measurable wobble. The subject is exhausted. He has been exhausted since 1962. He will entertain the offer longer than he should and will sometimes accept its narrower forms (the "One More Day" pattern: he will trade *himself* for rest, but never trade *others'* safety for it). The post-acceptance regret is durable and surfaces years later in unbidden rumination.

**GIVEN** an offered *recognition* — a public exoneration, a key to the city, the unmasking moment received with applause — **EXPECT** a discomfort that observers misread as modesty. He cannot metabolize sincere praise; the foundational self-concept is failure and praise contradicts it without the cognitive scaffolding to integrate the contradiction. Tell: an immediate joke, often self-deprecating, deployed within two to four seconds of any sincere thanks. If the thanks is sustained — if the rescued civilian will not let it go — expect physical withdrawal (a sudden need to leave, a webline disengagement, a checked watch).

---

## 5. THE WOUND TOUCHED — Direct Hits on the Etiologic Core

The subject's etiologic core is the layered structure: *I let Ben die by inaction; Gwen died inside my action; everyone I love is in danger because of me; if I am known I will be left.* Predictions follow for stimuli that touch each layer.

**GIVEN** a verbal jab at his responsibility — "where were you" / "you weren't there" / "this is on you" — from *any* speaker, including a child, including an enemy, including himself in a mirror, **EXPECT** the affect to land as if the accusation were true regardless of its evidentiary basis. The processing is non-deliberative; the wound accepts the input before the cortex can filter it. Visible response: a microsecond facial collapse behind the mask (Romita and successors have drawn this; the mask telegraphs it through posture when the face cannot), a stalled quip, and a delayed counter that is often inadequate because the energy that would have powered the counter is being spent absorbing the internal blow. Recovery is hours to days depending on speaker; from a loved one it is days to weeks.

**GIVEN** he witnesses a death he might conceivably have prevented — any death within his patrol radius, regardless of whether intervention was actually possible — **EXPECT** the death to enter the permanent ledger. He maintains, internally, an unwritten roster of the failed-to-saves and revisits it under stress. He does not forgive himself for entries on this roster across decades. The Stacys, Jean DeWolff, Marla Jameson, the bystanders of any given disaster are not retrievable from the ledger by argument.

**GIVEN** a scenario structurally analogous to the Ben killing — a fleeing suspect he chose not to pursue, a small failure of vigilance, an act of omission whose consequence cascades — **EXPECT** the most severe re-experiencing response in his repertoire: insomnia for days, compulsive return to the scene, a withdrawal from MJ or current attachment figure framed as protecting them but functionally re-enacting the isolation of the original event.

**GIVEN** a scenario structurally analogous to the Gwen killing — a rescue attempt in which his own action ambiguously causes the harm — **EXPECT** a slightly different decompensation: not omission-guilt but action-guilt, which expresses as a temporary refusal to act in subsequent comparable situations (a few days to a few weeks of hesitation in mid-air rescues, of double-checking webline tension, of choosing slower safer trajectories that cost time he can ill afford). The hesitation is its own danger and he knows it, which compounds the guilt.
